The Vajrasattva Practice with Commentary
(1) Visualisation
First recite:
OM SVABHAVA SHUDDHA SARVA DHARMA SVABHAVA
SHUDDHO HAM
All phenomena including oneself enter the natural state of
emptiness.
The purpose of this mantra is to purify all appearances into the pure natural
state of emptiness, the ultimate truth which is empty of all deceptive
phenomena. You should visualise your body and all appearances as an.
empty reflection, like the reflection of the moon on a lake.
From the natural state of emptiness, above your crown the syllable
OM appears which is transformed into an eight-petalled white lotus
flower.
The syllable AH appears on top of the lotus flower and is transformed
into a full moon disc.
On top of the moon disc appears the syllable HUM, which then
transforms into a white five-pronged vajra with a HUM syllable at
its hub.
MA
.
.
1
Vajra
Slowly the natural state of emptiness becomes alive like the reflection
of a mirror, and from this appears the syllable OM (representing the
body of all the Buddhas), transforming into a white lotus flower which
symbolises the birth of your pure nature. The syllable AH represents
the speech of all the Buddhas while the full moon disc is a symbol of
225



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
-
compassion. The syllable HUM represents the mind of all the Buddhas,
and the vajra (as shown above) represents indestructible, unyielding
spiritual power and wisdom. The vajra is usually made from metal and
has five prongs at each end, representing the five Buddha-families or five
wisdoms of a Buddha29.
To unveil the dharmakaya or natural Buddha within us, we need to
accumulate merit and purify all defilements on a relative level. The
lotus, vajra and the seed syllables thus represent the generation of merit
and the process of purification during the different stages of existence –
birth, natural life, death, bardo30 and rebirth.
This HUM radiates luminous light to all universes and makes
limitless offerings to all Arya beings.
The light then radiates back to all beings and purifies their
defilements.
It then returns and dissolves into the syllable HUM, and the white
five-pronged vajra then completely melts into light.
The HUM syllable is the essence of the mind of all the Buddhas. When
you radiate light making offerings to all Arya beings you are invoking
the blessings of all the Buddhas, and visualising the light of these
blessings dissolving back into you is a tantric way to make the practice
powerful. You then purify the defilements of all beings with this same
light, which is a unique method of accumulating merit. The purpose
of making limitless offerings to enlightened beings and purifying the
defilments of sentient beings is to attain the rupakaya form body, which
'is the result of the accumulation of merit. Without making offerings to
noble beings and purifying the defilements of all sentient beings, we will
never achieve complete enlightenment.
The light then transforms instantly into Vajrasattva, with a white
body, one face and two arms, holding a vajra in his right hand and
a bell in his left.
He embraces the consort Vajra Bhagavati in Yab-yum.
29 The five wisdoms include the wisdom of all-accomplishing space, the mirror-
like wisdom, the wisdom of equanimity, the wisdom of perfect discrimination and the
all-accomplishing wisdom.
30 ‘Bardo' refers to the transition period between death and one's next rebirth
- see chapter 24 of Unveiling Your Sacred Truth – The Sixfold Cycle of Life, Death and
Rebirth.
226



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
The form of Vajrasattva and Vajra Bhagavati is the rupakaya aspect of
enlightement in this practice, which represents all the merit you need to
accumulate so that you can spontaneously benefit others.
Vajrasattva has a radiant white body which is youthful, translucent,
perfectly proportioned and attractive – these features symbolise the
purification of all defilements. In Vajrayana, attributes like the vajra
and bell are particular "conditions' to link you with the qualities of
enlightenment, and this works on the principle of interdependence. The
vajra embodies the quality of being indestructible, just like a diamond,
and represents the Buddha's mind.
The bell, bearing the image of a Buddha's face and the inscription of a
mantra, represents the enlightened body and speech. The vajra is also
the symbol of spontaneous great bliss and masculine spiritual qualities
such as compassion. The bell also represents empty form and feminine
spiritual qualities, especially wisdom.
Although the practice still works if you visualise Vajrasattva by himself,
it is more effective to visualise Vajrasattva together with his consort
Vajra Bhagavati in enlightened embrace. This is known as Vajrasattva
Yab-yum, and signifies the union of masculine and feminine qualities in
the ultimate state.
Vajra Bhagavati is white in colour, holding a curved knife in her
right hand and a skull cup in her left.
They are both adorned with silk and jewel ornaments with legs
crossed in the vajra-lotus posture.
Great bliss manifests from their enlightened embrace.
The curved knife signifies method, or the ability to cut though the dualistic
mind, while the skull cup represents wisdom, or the “consumption' of
impure dualistic thought. Both Vajrasattva and Vajra Bhagavati are
adorned with five silk garments and eight jewel ornaments.
The five silken garments include: (1) a patterned blue silk scarf, (2) five
coloured crown pendants, (3) a white silk upper-garment, (4) a lower skirt-
like garment, and (5) long sleeves. These symbolise the five wisdoms.
The eight jewel ornaments include: (1) a crown, (2) earrings, (3-5) short,
middle and long necklaces, (6) shoulder ornaments, (7) bracelets and (8)
227



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
anklets. These signify the eight pure consciousnesses31.
2
.
-.-
The crossing of their legs in the vajra-lotus posture symbolises the
indivisibility of samsara and nirvana, and great bliss arises from the
inseparable union of their enlightened embrace.
At their forehead is OM.
At their throat is AH.
At their heart is HUM.
At their navel is HO.
From the HUM at their heart, light radiates outward to the ten
directions and the purification power of all the Buddhas and
bodhisattvas radiates back in the form of white nectar.
The OM, AH and HUM syllables at the forehead, throat and heart
represent the indestructible body, speech and mind of Vajrasattva, while
HO at the navel signifies indestructible primordial wisdom. The light
radiating to all the Buddhas and bodhisattvas collects their blessings
and empowers the heart of Vajrasattva with the purification power of
all the Buddhas (which Vajrasattva represents). This takes the form of
luminous, translucent, milky-white nectar, sometimes called bodhicitta
nectar, and this flows forth from of the HUM at Vajrasattva's heart, as
if it was sweating.
DZA HUM BAM HO.
The nectar now becomes inseparable with Vajrasattva Yab-yum.
With DZA the nectar is drawn above the crown of Vajrasattva, with HUM
it dissolves into Vajrasattva, and with BAM it flows into Vajrasattva Yab-
yum. Finally, as HO is recited the nectar becomes completely inseparable
with Vajrasattva Yab-yum. Having completely filled Vajrasattva and
consort, the nectar overflows from every pore of their body, especially
their secret place, and cascades downwards like a waterfall or a gentle
shower of rain.
SO
'Vajrasattva, please purify and cleanse all the negativity,
obscurations and downfalls accumulated by myself and all beings
since beginningless time'
31 These include the purified forms of the consciousnesses of: eye, ear,
nose, tongue, body, mind, deluded mind and foundation consciousness. In Vajrayana
Buddhism this is equivalent to the eight bodhisattvas.
228



---

HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
With this verse you are calling on Vajrasattva (or Vajrasattva Yab-yum)
to purify and cleanse all your negativity; obscurations and downfalls.
The powers of support, regret and resolution are included here - you
are recalling all the negative actions, habits and bad energies of your
body, speech and mind, asking Vajrasattva for forgiveness and vowing
never to do them again. You then visualise the nectar flowing through
your body from your crown and forehead, pushing down all sicknesses,
bad energies and other defilements, which leave your body in the form
of black liquid, blood and pus through your lower orifices. You can also
expand your visualisation to include all beings since beginningless time,
thinking that their defilements are being purified at the same time as
your own32
While all this is going on you should begin to recite the Vajrasattva
mantra, as shown below:
(ii) The Actual Purification
[While visualising blissful nectar flowing from the union of Vajrasattva Yab-yum.
and bringing to mind the four powers, recite the following mantra):
OM

that follows].
N
This mantra connects you to the divine healing power of Vajrasattva
and makes the cleansing process more effective than the visualisation
alone, provided you invoke all of the four powers and you have good
single-pointed concentration. There are many options for what to make
the centre of your attention while doing this practice. You can choose
to focus, for example, on the meaning of the mantra, on your feeling of
regret and resolve, on the form of Vajrasattva Yab-yum or on the flow
of nectar through your subtle body. If you are overwhelmed by all these
details, the most important thing is to recall the four powers and simply
try to feel Vajrasattva's presence. It may also be possible to use a shorter
version of the mantra - OM VAJRASATTVA HUM.

HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH

-
When you are focusing on the Vajrasattva practice, you should dedicate
formal sessions to accumulating the long mantra. The goal is to
accumulate 100,000 mantras, which usually takes about three months
when the practice. is done intensively, though in reality you should
practice until signs of purification appear33.
Great protector, due to ignorance and confusion I have broken my
samaya and let them decline.
Compassionate Lama Vajrasattva, please purify my negativities and
protect me.
In you I take refuge, supreme vajra holder, treasure of compassion
and rescuer of all beings.
You are now confessing all the occasions when you have broken your
commitments or let them decline, whether you are aware of this or not
due to ignorance and confusion. This mainly refers to samaya, which are
vows to view the lama as someone sacred and to have pure perception of
all phenomena (for example, to regard everything as the pure display of
the Kalachakra mandala). This is mostly relevant to those who have an
authentic Vajrayana relationship with their teacher and should not be a
source of unnecessary guilt. This verse can also apply to the bodhisattva
vows you may have broken, as well as more basic precepts you may
have taken34
In the first part of the verse you are invoking the power of regret, thinking
intensely of all the negativity, you have accumulated, and then in the
second part you are re-invoking the power of support by praying to
compassionate Lama Vajrasattva and taking refuge in him. At the same
time you are applying the power of action, as by reciting this prayer you
are creating positive energy that will counteract the negativity
33 Certain signs may appear in dreams, such as your body being purified by
water or pus and sweat coming out of your body. They can also appear in life, such as
your body becoming very light or your mind becoming sharp and clear.
34 You should remember that it is only human to take vows, break them and then
have to purify them again. As a beginner it takes some time to “get used to’keeping
these vows, and you should decide to keep the level of vows which best matches your
own capacity, whether this be vinaya precepts, bodhisattva commitments or tantric
vows. The three vows are discussed more fully in chapter twenty-one of Unveiling
Your Sacred Truth: Tantric Vows and Pledges.
231



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
of your previous actions.
I confess all downfalls of my body, speech and mind, including all
breaches of my root and branch vows.
Please purify and cleanse all the stains, downfalls and negative
obscurations amassed during beginningless time in samsara.
This is similar to the previous verse, only here you specifically recollect
all your downfalls of body, speech and mind, as well as all breaches of
root and branch vows. In the Kalachakra Tantra there are fourteen root
vows and eighteen branch vows. To be qualified to keep tantric vows,
however, you must also keep bodhisattva vows to the best of your ability,
which include eighteen root vows and forty-six branch vows35.
Finally you exhort Vajrasattva once again to purify and cleanse all
the stains, downfalls and negative obscurations amassed during
beginningless time in samsara. We have developed many strong habits
over countless lifetimes, and we are relying on Vajrasattva to help peel
back layer upon layer of these habitual patterns – to purify all our negative
emotions, negative deeds and tendencies to break promises, as well as
intellectual obscurations which prevent us from seeing ultimate truth.
At this point you should also generate a strong resolve to never again
be taken over by these negative habits and to refrain from committing
negative deeds even if your life is at stake (the power of resolution).
Vajrasattva Yab-yum looks at me with a smile and transforms into a
white moon, dissolving through the crown of my head.
The body, speech and mind of Vajrasattva Yab-yum become
inseparable from my own body, speech and mind.
Having completed the relative practice of purification, Vajrasattva then
looks at you with a smile, as if to say “well done'. He then dissolves into
you, becoming inseparable from your own body speech and mind, as you
realise that on the ultimate level Vajrasattva is none other than your own
Buddha-nature. You thus recognise that you were always a Buddha.
When you focus on accumulating the Vajrasattva mantra, it is good to
practice dissolving and then re-visualising at regular intervals,
35
The Bodhisattva vows are described in chapter fourteen of Unveiling
Your Sacred Truth: Bodhicitta - The Unique and Extraordinary Mahayana Altruistic
Intention.
232



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
for example at the end of each mala. This reminds you of the empty nature
of the visualisation and prevents you from being fixated on appearance,
as you watch the inseparability of you and Vajrasattva again and again.
(iii) Dedication of virtue
Through this virtue may I quickly reach the enlightened state of
Vajrasattva and lead all beings without exception to this ground of
purity.
Through this virtue may all beings complete the accumulation
of merit and primordial wisdom and so attain the two kayas of
enlightenment.
This dedication is similar to the prayer you recîte at the end of the previous
practices. This time, however, the emphasis is on the purity aspect of
enlightenment so you aspire to reach the enlightened state of Vajrasattva
and lead all beings to this state as well. Once they attain enlightenment
they will have attained the two Buddha-kayas, the dharmakaya truth
body and the rupakaya form body, which are the result of accumulating
wisdom and merit respectively.
233



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
IV. Mandala Offering
Introduction
The purpose of the mandala offering practice is to accumulate merit by
making the vastest possible offering with the best possible motivation,
to most the worthy possible recipient – the sublime Three Jewels. Merit
is the positive energy you create by doing good deeds, and this becomes
the cause for good things to happen to you in the future. If you are
generous, for example, the result is wealth, and if you are patient the
result is a beautiful appearance. With the motivation of enlightenment,
the result can be circumstances and opportunities which help you on
your spiritual path. Merit can also increase your ability to understand the
Dharma correctly, be enthusiastic about your practice and take obstacles
as a blessing.
During the mandala offering you symbolically offer the centre and
circumference of the entire universe to enlightened beings in the form
of a picture or collection of objects, both real and visualised. There are
many different ways to represent mandalas, such as sand mandalas,
picture mandalas or three-dimensional mandalas 36. They can also be
simply represented by piles of jewels, stones or rice. The traditional
long mandala offering is done in various layers upon a circular base,
with rings surrounding each layer. The short mandala offering, which
you accumulate when you are focusing on this practice, involves
placing seven heaps of rice upon a plate which dissolve as you offer the
mandala.
The rice or jewels that you offer represent all the precious things in
this world, all the merit you and others have ever accumulated and all
enlightened realms as well – in short, everything you can possibly think
of. You then offer this mandala to the entire field of refuge, including the
36 For a more in-depth discussion of what a mandala is, as well as the
principles of mandala offering, see chapter seventeen of Unveiling Your Sacred Truth:
The Sublime Universal Mandala Offering.
234



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
root lama and all the Buddhas, bodhisattvas and so forth. Finally you
request that your offerings are accepted for the liberation of all beings,
and if you are doing a long offering you can place this on an altar in front
of your shrine.
W
We now describe the mandala offering practice according to the Jonang
tradition, remembering that as with any practice you should first take
refuge and then generate the mind of bodhicitta.
The Mandala Offering

(i) Invoking the Field of
Merit
You are the jewel-like lama,
The one whose kindness leads
to the dawning of great bliss in
a single instant.
I bow to your lotus feet, Lama Vajradhara.
----www-wwwwwwwwwwww
This and the following two verses are a special invocation of the field
of merit which you are making the offering to, and this is embodied
by the jewel-like lama who is your human link with enlightenment and
represents the Three Jewels. The lama is especially remembered for his
kindness, as the kindness of our human teachers is said to surpass even
that of the great Buddhas, who are currently unable to help us directly
due to our lack of merit. Thinking of the lama can lead to the dawning
of great bliss in a single instant when your gratitude and devotion take
you beyond your ordinary conceptual mind. Although we say ‘lama'
235



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
(singular), we should remember that this can represent one teacher or
many, both male and female, so long as they have benefited you on your
journey to enlightenment.
Bowing to the lama's lotus feet is a poetic way to say that every part
of the lama's body possesses great beauty, and secondly it refers to the
lotus flower as a seat upon which the lama sits, as described in various
visualisations. In Buddhist culture it is seen as a great honour to touch
the lowest point of the lama’s body (the feet) with the highest point of
your own body. We refer to the lama as Lama Vajradhara, whose form
we have previously visualised in the refuge practice, as his enlightened
body is indestructible and he represents the dharmakaya truth body of
enlightenment.
I pay homage to the lama for whom
my gratitude is beyond compare.
The light of your enlightened truth dispels my darkness.
You are the faultless wisdom eye, the sun-like lama of great bliss.
According to Vajrayana Buddhism, your spiritual progress depends
on your ability to show gratitude and appreciation for your lama and
the light of his enlightened truth, which is the truth you discover by
practising the Dharma he teaches. The faultless wisdom eye refers to the
lama's ability to see and point out our hidden weaknesses, while sun-like
means the lama is like a source of radiant light; enabling us to see all that
is around us.
You are our mother and father.
You are the master of all beings, a true
and noble friend and protector.
You are the great rescuer who steals away negative obscurations.
You are the one abiding in excellence,
The sole abode of all supreme qualities,
completely free from all faults.
You are the protector of the lowly, supreme conqueror
of self-cherishing and suffering;
The source of all wealth, the wish-fulfilling jewel.
The Dharma teacher is like a parent in a spiritual sense - like a
father he guides and protects you on your spiritual journey, and like
a mother he provides you with love and spiritual nourishment. He is
the master of all beings as he does not discriminate who he will guide
236



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
to enlightenment and he accepts all beings regardless of caste, race
or social standing. As a noble friend he shares the precious Dharma
with you and provides unconditional love and support, caring for you
until you reach enlightenment. Furthermore, he protects you from the
suffering of samsara and the cycle of existence and rescues or benefits
you by showing you how to achieve enlightened qualities.
In addition, the Dharma teacher steals away negative obscurations
by teaching you how to overcome all negative qualities, and it is only
by following his teachings that you can attain the supreme qualities
of Buddhahood. As a manifestation of the Buddhas in human form,
the lama is also the protector of lowly and deprived beings and is the
supreme conqueror of self-cherishing and suffering, having achieved
enlightenment for the sake of all beings. Finally, he is described as a
wish-fulfilling jewel as he is able to manifest limitless enlightened
qualities for the benefit of his followers.
In you I take refuge, immaculate and holy root lama,
Embodiment of the Buddhas of the three times.
[This verse is a shortened version of the previous three verses and may be used on its
own].
You can recite this verse alone instead of the previous three verses,
recalling that taking refuge in the Three Jewels is the foundation of all
Dharma practice. Here taking refuge in the lama is equal to taking refuge
in the Three Jewels, as the lama is considered the embodiment of the
Buddhas of the three times, the past, present and future. All past Buddhas
achieved enlightenment through reliance on their Dharma teachers, all
present Buddhas manifest in the form of Dharma teachers and all future
Buddhas are trained by Dharma teachers. This is why the lama, who
teaches you the precious Dharma, is seen as holy and immaculate.
(ii) Medium-length Mandala Offering
OM VAJRA BHUMI AH HUM
The foundation is the pure golden earth.
Here we begin the medium-length mandala offering practice unique to
the Jonang tradition. This involves placing nine heaps of rice or jewels
237



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
7
on a plate, which represents the universe being offered to the field of
refuge. This is much briefer than the traditional long mandala offering
which involves thirty-seven offering objects.
With the mantra OM VAJRA BHUM AH HUM you are beginning to
assemble the mandala by creating a foundation, the pure golden earth,
on which you can build a physical and mental picture of the universe. A
circular golden plate is used to represent this foundation, and you should
rub its surface with your wrist before proceeding with the offering.
OM means “perfect or ‘with excellence', and is used at the beginning of
any activity to help guide us to perfection.
VAJRA means “indestructible.'
BHUMI means “the earth’.
AH means “fundamental origin' or 'emptiness.'
HUM means 'essential' or 'fullness.
Taken together, this mantra leads us to excellence and glory in any
activity and assists us in reaching enlightenment.
The model for the universe that we are using here is a little different
from the conventional scientific model. According to the Kalachakra
Tantra, the universe was formed as the four great elements coalesced
according to the collective karma of beings. The black wind was first
to arise, followed by the red fire element, the white water element and
finally the yellow earth element, which all appear as concentric discs
with decreasing diameter.
OM VAJRA REKHE AH HUM
The world is encircled by a great iron fence and in the centre is
Mount Meru, the king of mountains.
With this mantra you visualise the great Mount Meru appearing upon
the centre of the yellow earth disc, encircled by a great iron fence or
perimeter ridge which represents the outer boundary of the universe or
world system. Mount Meru is circular in shape,
and at its peak are five summits, as shown in the illustration below37.
37 For a more detailed description of the universe according to the Kalachakra
Tantra, see chapter seventeen of Unveiling Your Sacred Truth: The Sublime Universal
Mandala Offering.
238



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
At the same time you should place a heap of rice or jewels in the centre
of the golden plate and a ring around its perimeter, if you have one.

These are the four
continents surrounding
Mount Meru. To the
east is Luphagpo
(meaning great
physical prosperity'),
with three islands
in the shape of semi-circles. To the south is Dzambuling, (a place of
the sound Dzam -likened to the sound of tree leaves falling into the
sea) with three triangular islands. This is where our planet is said to be
located and is the only region where the Dharma is currently known. To
the north is Draminyen (meaning ‘hidden news and bad sound'), with
three circular islands, and to the west is Balangchod (meaning ‘great
material prosperity'), with three square islands. It is difficult to say how
the description of these continents relates to modern-day geographical
knowledge. However, it probably describes a more subtle dimension
beyond what we normally know as the physical universe.
While you are visualising these four continents, you should place four
heaps of rice or jewels on the offering plate in a clockwise direction.
The sun, moon, rahu and kalagni, all things pleasing and prosperous
within the world of humans and gods, complete and lacking
nothing...
All this wealth I offer with great devotion to my immaculate root and
lineage lamas,
And to the mandala of yidams, Buddhas, bodhisattvas, pratyekas,
shravakas, dakinis and all-seeing dharma protectors.
With this verse you are offering everything in the universe you can
possibly think of, including the sun, moon and celestial bodies known
239



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
as rahu and kalagni in the Kalachakra Tantra, which all have profound
spiritual and astrological significance. The rahu, represented by a black
disc, appears during a lunar eclipse and is associated with the north node
of the moon, while the kalagni (a yellow disc) appears during a solar
eclipse and is associated with the south node of the moon.
While it is good to know the traditional cosmology and visualise the
universe in this way, you should also be creative with this practice and
bring to mind everything that is pleasing in the world of humans and
gods, including lakes, forests, mountains, palaces, jewels and works of
art. You could also offer Asia, South and North America, national parks,
waterfalls, money, flying carpets, video cameras, banks and even objects
of your mind such as virtuous qualities and spiritual attainments. We
may think the practice is a little fabricated as we are not actually offering
anything that belongs to us. However, our perception belongs to us, and
this is what we are offering – in fact everything in the universe is our
perception.
While mentally generating offering objects, you should continue to
offer heaps of rice or jewels in a clockwise direction, nine piles in all,
noting how the movement of rice is similar to the arising and dissolution
of thoughts in rapid succession. After placing these nine piles on the
offering plate, you should then hold up the plate as a gesture of offering
all this wealth with great devotion to the field of refuge, the immaculate
root and lineage lamas and so forth.
Out of compassion accept this mandala for the sake of all beings
And having accepted this offering, please bless me!
Having made this offering, you then ask the field of refuge to accept
this mandala. As the Buddhas' compassion is limitless, their blessings
will naturally arise in us when the offering is made. Our offering of
the universe should also include the merit accumulated by all sentient
beings and all enlightened beings. Offering in this way increases the
merit of all beings so that they may reach enlightenment, and therefore
the offering is made for the sake of all beings.
Recollecting the virtue of body, speech and mind gathered by myself
and all beings during the three times, together with the collection of
excellent offerings in this precious mandala;
I offer this all to my lama and the Three Jewels.

HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
-
Please accept this with your compassion and bless me!
The collection of virtue of the three times refers to merit that has been
accumulated with body, speech and mind since beginningless time,
as well as the merit generated now and in the future until we reach
buddhahood. As in the previous verse, you are asking the field of refuge,
which is embodied by the lama and the Three Jewels, to accept your
offering and bless your mind-stream, thus strengthening your spiritual
practice.
This is the final verse of the medium-length mandala offering, and if
you wish you can repeat these verses again and again, counting these
as accumulations. However, when focusing on accumulations it is more
common to use the brief seven-point offering as explained below.
(iii) Brief Mandala Offering
[This is an alternative briefer form of the mandala offering, which can be used for
accumulations)
The ground is anointed with perfume and strewn with flowers.
On it is placed Mt Meru and the four continents of the universe,
sun and moon.
This I offer as a buddha-field for all beings to enjoy.
IDAM GURU RATNA MANDALA KAM NIRYA TAYAMI
[Reciting this, offer the mandala].
This short version of the mandala offering is generally used for
accumulations, although it is good if you can recite the medium-length
version beforehand.
First you should clean the offering plate with your wrist in a clockwise
circular motion, and if you wish you can splash scented water on the
plate before doing this. This symbolises the ground being purified or
anointed with perfume and strewn with flowers. Then you place one heap
of rice in the centre, symbolising Mount Meru, followed by one heap in
the front, one to the left, one behind and one to the right. These last four
241



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
piles represent the four quarters of the universe or four continents. You
then end with two more piles - one between the left and centre piles
an one between the right and centre piles. These represent the sun and
moon.
The visualisation is similar to that described in the previous practice. In
particular, the base of the offering mandala is made of golden material and
anointed with perfume, representing the vast array of natural perfumes,
plants and flowers of this earth. You then visualise all sorts of pleasing
things such as jewels, crystals, flowers, herbs and grains, as well as the
sun, moon, rivers, lakes, minerals, creatures of all shapes and sizes and
other objects of natural beauty. Finally, you visualise this entire offering
transforming into a Buddha-field, a pure land inhabited by enlightened
beings with magnificent trees, palaces and special beings as in the refuge
practice. This Buddha-field has the power to benefit beings in limitless
ways, and so you offer this for all beings to enjoy.
After each recitation of the prayer you then recite the mantra IDAMGURU
RATNA MANDALA KAM NIRYA TAYAMI and consider the offering
mandala to dissolve into you. You then quickly clean the offering plate
and recite the prayer again as you place the seven heaps of rice on the
plate for the next offering. When you are accumulating this process is
repeated quite quickly. The shortest possible way is to simply repeat the
mantra while you are creating and then dissolving the mandala, though
it is important that you are always aware of the meaning of the practice
as you do this. You can also alternate this brief offering with the longer
version, for example doing one longer offering after twenty-five of the
shorter ones.
242



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
V. Foundation Guru Yoga
Introduction
The purpose of guru yoga, the fifth Kalachakra preliminary, is to unify
your mind with the holy mind of your teachers. On a relative level you
chant all kinds of prayers and supplications to open your mind and heart
to the lama's blessings and generate great devotion. On an ultimate level
you learn to recognise that the ultimate lama is none other than your
own wisdom mind. This means the lama is not only an important person,
but is your personal path to enlightenment. As we are unable to receive
direct guidance from enlightenment beings, we need to rely on a human
to link us to the enlightened wisdom of the Buddha. This outer teacher is
the person you hire to do the job of dismantling your ego, and this leads
to the discovery of the inner teacher, your own enlightened wisdom. The
practice of guru yoga is absolutely essential if you wish to follow the
tantric path to enlightenment,
as it is the lama's blessing that allows you to develop pure perception
and opens the door to all tantric realisations38. If you have a sceptical
mind, you might be very suspicious of the whole idea of guru devotion
- it may seem like something fabricated, theistic or undemocratic. On
a basic level Buddhism is all about good logic and practical methods
that everyone can easily test, which is like the manual for driving a car.
However, practices like guru devotion and guru yoga take you beyond
this basic level of Buddhism - they are like the personal advice of a
driving instructor, containing key knowledge handed down about how to
practise effectively39. The inspirational verses of the guru yoga practice
are not just blind devotion - they are designed to deeply penetrate
38 The purpose of guru yoga and the importance of guru devotion is explained
in far greater detail in chapter eighteen of Unveiling Your Sacred Truth: Guru Yoga -
The. Gateway to Tantric Realisation.
39 These key practical instructions are an important part of any transmission
lineage. They are also known as pith instructions or heart advice.
243



..
...
.-
BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
your mind-stream and lead you to an understanding of truth beyond
all words and concepts. You should remember that real guru devotion
is not a theistic or dictatorial situation, but rather an honouring of the
mutual agreement between yourself and your teacher to work towards
enlightenment.

i
The practice which follows is the first of three guru yoga practices
performed in the Jonang tradition. In this practice you focus on the
root lama inseparable from Vajradhara, while in the other two practices
you focus on the two most important Jonang lineage masters, Dolpopa
and Taranatha. To begin with you must generate the altruistic mind of
bodhicitta, as in any Mahayana practice. You then commence the guru
244



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
yoga practice, which takes place in four sequential stages – visualisation,
supplicating the lama (and the lineage masters), receiving the four
empowerments and finally mixing your mind with the lama's wisdom
mind.
The Guru Yoga Practice with Commentary
(0) Visualisation
Visualise yourself in a magnificent vast palace in the centre of a pure
realm. Picture your vajra master as Lord Vajradhara seated above
you and facing the same direction, in the centre of the palace upon a
lion throne, sitting upon a lotus, sun disc and moon disc.
Visualise the vajra master as having a body blue in colour, one
face, two arms, holding a vajra and bell crossed at the level of his
heart. His legs are in full lotus posture. Adorned with silk and jewel
ornaments, with the marks and signs complete, his body is radiant
and luminous and he is smiling in your direction, pleased with you.
He is surrounded by the lineage lamas and the entire assembly of
yidam deities, Buddhas, bodhisattvas, shravakas, pratyekas, dakinis
and dharma protectors. Be confident that all of them are actually
present.
.
The guru yoga practice begins by invoking your lama, the vajra master,
in the divine form of Lord Vajradhara, who is the embodiment of all the
lineage masters, Buddhas, bodhisattvas and so forth. As in the refuge
practice, you consider that all appearances dissolve into emptiness,
from which a pure realm with a magnificent vast palace emerges like
the reflection of the full moon in a lake. The lama then appears in the
space in front of you as the primordial Buddha Vajradhara upon the lion
throne, lotus, sun and moon disc, and he gazes affectionately at you,
signifying your close personal connection with him. The details of the
assembly's make-up and the significance of each type of enlightened
being are described in the refuge section. Unlike the assembly in the
refuge visualisation, in this practice the field of enlightened beings is
gathered like a crowd surrounding your root lama.
245



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
Your visualisation should be clear, vivid and vibrant, yet appearing like a
reflection as none of the visualised objects have a truly existing external
nature. If they are familiar to you, it might also help to recall some of
the stories of the great lineage masters to bring this to life. As with any
visualisation practice, you should try to visualise the objects as best
you can. However, the details are not as important as the feeling of the
practice or the meaning behind it.
Having made great offerings, both actual and visualised, make the
following request with sincere and confident faith.
Having visualised the field of assembly, you then visualise making great
offerings to Lama Vajradhara and his enlightened companions. You can
also make actual offerings to the lama, for example, by placing precious
objects in front of a shrine. On a more practical level, you can pledge to
offer the lama your time, services, monetary assistance or other kinds of
help according to your capacity.
As you begin the practice you should have sincere and confident
faith, which is total trust in the truth of the path you are following,
being convinced that you possess Buddha-nature and that this can be
uncovered. Faith is essentially trust in the process of cause, condition and
effect. Just as you can know with confidence that you can bake a cake
if all the right ingredients are present, so too can you be confident in the
enlightened path when certain conditions are present. These conditions
include renunciation, compassion, devotion and above all knowing that
you possess the Buddha-nature.
(ii) Prayers to the Lineage Masters
Kind and precious lama,
Everything good and virtuous in samsara and nirvana
Has arisen from your enlightened power.
My protector, source of every conceivable benefit,
I pray to you from the depths of my heart.
According to Vajrayana Buddhism, your kind and precious lama, whose
nature is inseparable from all the Buddhas, is the source of everything
conceivable that is virtuous, good and beneficial. Although he is equal
246



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
to the great Buddhas in his wisdom, his kindness surpasses that of the
Buddhas as he is appearing to you right now. Remembering his great
kindness, including all circumstances when his teachings helped you
and all the small acts of kindness and compassion you can recall, you
should pray to him from the depths of your heart. In doing so you are
actually invoking the wisdom aspect of your own mind.
I pray to the all-pervasive truth body of great bliss,
The primordial Buddha Vajradhara who abides in Akanishta.
I pray to Kalachakra the enjoyment body.
I pray to Buddha Shakyamuni the emanation body.
I pray to you who embodies all of the four Buddha-kayas.
The lineage that the root lama embodies begins with the primordial Buddha
Vajradhara, whose form represents the all-pervasive dharmakaya truth
body of enlightenment, which is changeless and beyond form. Akanishta
literally means the highest', and in this case it refers to the enlightened
sphere of dharmakaya Buddha, the realm of Vajradhara40. Kalachakra
represents the samboghakaya enjoyment body of enlightenment, while
Buddha Shakyamuni represents the emanation body, which together are
the compassionate display of enlightened energy for the sake of others.
We pray to the lama who embodies the four Buddha-kayas, which include
the above three kayas as well as the svabhavikakaya, which is the union
of these three.
I pray to the Dharma Kings , translators and panditas;
The thirty-five Shambala Kings, emanations of the victorious ones,
The two Dushapas and the two unsurpassed scholars,
Nalendrapa and Drolway Gonpo.
This verse connects us to some of the most important masters in the
Jonang-Shambala lineage. The Dharma Kings, translators and panditas
include the thirty-five Shambala Kings of the Kalachakra dynasty, the
two Dushapas (who brought the Kalachakra teachings into the human
world), and two great scholars of the. Jonang lineage, Nalendrapa (abbot
of the great Nalanda University) and Drolway Gonpo, more commonly
known as Taranatha. Taranatha, who is one of the most important Jonang
masters, composed over forty texts,

including material based on the recollection of his previous lives.
I pray to the three lamas who attained supreme siddhis:
Protector of all beings Konchoksung,
Great and accomplished meditator Droton Namseg
Great yogi Drupchen Yumo Chöki Rachen.
We now begin invoking the lineage lamas in sets of three, in rough

siddhis refers to extraordinary spiritual attainment. Konchoksung,
also known as Lama Lhaje Gompa, was a great nagpa (tantric lay
practitioner) who spread the Kalachakra teachings widely. Droton
Namseg, also a nagpa, is said to have developed a direct connection
with many enlightened deities through exceptional meditation practice.
Drupchen Yumo Chöki Rachen was a fully ordained monk famed for his
extraordinary spiritual powers, and therefore a great yogi.

Seachok Dharmeshvara,
Flawless Dharma scholar Kipa Namkha Od,

Seachok Dharmeshvara was hailed as an emanation of Manjushri and
was the son of Drupchen Yumo. Kipa Namkha Od (Khipa Namkha Öser)
was an extraordinary, flawless scholar and great tantric yogi who was a
master of Asanga's work as well as the Kalachakra Tantra. Semochen
(Lama Drubtop Sechen) achieved swift realisation after practicing the
Six Vajra Yogas, and thus gained clairvoyance and other supernatural

All-knowing Kunkhyen Chöku Öser,

Jamsar Sherab (also known as Chöje Jamyang Sarma) was a highly
realised master who was healed from leprosy after engaging in extensive
retreat practice. Chöku Öser was a great scholar of the sutras and tantras,
hailed as omniscient or all-knowing, and was also a highly accomplished
yogi. Kunphang Tukje Tsondu was regarded as an emanation of one of
the Shambal Rigden Kings, having unified many of the Kalachakra
lineages in Tibet and perfected immutable bliss through the practice of
the Six Vajra Yogas.

Khetsun Zangpo (also known as Khetsun Yonten Gyatso) was known

Jonang luminary Dolpopa, who unified the Kalachakra Tantra and
Shentong sutra lineages, was considered the emanation of the Buddha of
the three times as his realisation and mastery of the Buddha's teachings
was so profound as both a scholar and a saint.

Flourishing in the continent with the wisdom of Manjushri, Jamphel

Tenpa Rabgye received all the instructions for the Six Vajra Yogas from
Ngawang Chözin and experienced many signs indicating mastery of
the practice. He lived a very humble life and at 76 years passed away,
remaining in a state of clear light for six days. Lobsang Trinley also
focused intensively on the Kalachakra practice. After contracting leprosy
in his thirties and entering into a solitary retreat to practice Vajrapani for
five years, he dedicated the remainder of his life to treating and curing
people with leprosy and other illnesses. He also worked tirelessly to to
rebuild Mahayana and Vajrayana Buddhism in its pure form. Jamphel
Lodro was recognised as the reincarnation of Getse Khentrul who in his
previous life was the Kalachakra master, Chozin Gyatso. He studied the
five Tibetan Buddhist traditions through attending eleven monasteries in
Tibet. After a pilgrimage to India to practice at the major sacred Buddhist
sites, he travelled to Australia with a dedicated commitment to teach and
translate the Dharma into the English language.
(iii) Seven-limb Prayer & Supplication
I prostrate with body, speech and mind to you, supreme
and unfailing refuge.
I offer limitless clouds of offerings, both real
and mentally generated.
This verse is the beginning of what is known as the seven-branch
practice. In the Tibetan Buddhist tradition this collection of seven
prayers is commonly recited as a preliminary to many practices, as it
offers a condensed version of many instructions which are essential to
the accumulation of merit and wisdom.
The first is similar to the refuge practice, in which you prostrate with
body, speech and mind as a way of paying homage and expressing respect
to the supreme and unfailing refuge of the lama and the Three Jewels,
who have the power to liberate you and all beings from samsara. This
acts as an antidote to our pride. The second part of the prayer involves
offering limitless clouds of offerings, both real and mentally generated,
as a way to accumulate merit. While reciting these prayers you should
252



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
visualise the field of refuge as described above, with you and all sentient
beings offering prostrations and other precious objects as in the mandala
offering practice. This serves as an antidote to our stinginess or lack of
generosity.
I confess all my negativities and downfalls. .
I rejoice in all virtue within samsara and nirvana.
I pray that you turn the wheel of Dharma unceasingly.
The third branch of the seven-limb practice involves confessing all our
negativities and downfalls with the lama and Three Jewels as our witness.
As in the Vajrasattva practice, all four powers should be present. With
the lama and Three Jewels as your support, you should cultivate genuine
regret for all the negativity you have accumulated through your body,
speech and mind, as if you have just swallowed. poison, and resolve not
to repeat this in the future. As an antidote you can visualise light rays
emanating from the Three Jewels and washing away all your negativity,
gathered together in the form of a black pile on the tip of your tongue.
After this practice of confession, you then rejoice in all virtue within.
samsara and nirvana, which includes all the merit accumulated by
yourself and others, both ordinary sentient beings and enlightened
beings. This enables you to accumulate great waves of merit and acts as
an antidote to jealousy.
Next you pray that (the lama and the Three Jewels) turn the wheel of
Dharma unceasingly, as without someone to teach us Dharma there
would be no way to achieve liberation from samsara and we would be
like a blind person left alone in the middle of a desert. After attaining
enlightenment the Buddha initially decided not to teach, yet he changed
his mind when the gods Brahma and Indra made offerings and requested
him to turn the wheel of Dharma. In the same way we should request
that all those who hold the Buddha's teachings continue to teach in this
world as an antidote to our delusion.
I implore you to remain with us without passing into paranirvana.
May all virtue be dedicated so that
all beings swiftly attain supreme enlightenment!
253



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
Having prayed that the lama and Three Jewels turn the wheel of
Dharma, in this sixth branch we pray that they continue to remain with
us in samsara forever without passing into paranirvana, which is the
state beyond all suffering which the Buddha entered when he passed
away. Although in reality Buddha is beyond birth and death, our ability
to perceive him depends on our merit, so by making this request we are
praying that we will have the merit to keep on receiving his teachings.
The seventh and final branch of this practice is dedication, through
which we offer up all virtue so that all beings swiftly attain supreme
enlightenment. As with previous dedication practices, you should offer
up not only your own virtue, but all merit accumulated by yourself and
others throughout the past, present and future. This vast intention will no
doubt lead to a vast result.
[This seven-branch prayer was composed by Vakindadharma).
The above seven-branch prayer is actually a later addition to the original
guru yoga practice composed by Taranatha, as it was composed by
Vakindadharma.
I pray to my precious glorious lama, lord of Dharma and
embodiment of all the Buddhas.
I pray to my glorious lama, lord of Dharma possessing
the four Buddha-kayas.
This verse reminds us again how in Vajrayana practice the lama is the
most important object of refuge, as he is the embodiment of all the
Buddhas, or our living link with the universal energy of enlightenment.
By learning to see the lama as an enlightened being possessing the four
Buddha-kayas4l, we have a path by which to discover the inner four kayas
of our enlightened nature. Remember that ‘lama' does not necessarily
refer to one root teacher, but rather all the teachers who have helped you
on the path to enlightenment. You will then have most gratitude to one
or more of these teachers according to the karmic connection you have
41 The four kayas include: the dharmakaya (truth body), the samboghakaya
(enjoyment body), the nirmanakaya (emanation body) and the svabhavikakaya (the
union of these three). We can also speak of the three kayas (the first three together) or
the two kayas, the dharmakaya and rupakaya (or form body, which is the enjoyment
body and emanation body together).
254



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
with them.
I pray to my precious glorious lama, lord of Dharma,
my unequalled supreme refuge.
I pray to my precious glorious lama, lord of Dharma,
my unequalled rescuer.
The lama is your unequalled supreme refuge and unequalled rescuer as
he embodies the supreme refuge of the Three Jewels, who offer us an
unmistaken and unequalled path by which we can be rescued from the
suffering of samsara and attain perfect enlightenment.
I pray to my precious glorious lama, lord of Dharma, who teaches
the supreme path to liberation. I pray to my precious glorious lama,
lord of Dharma, the source of all sublime qualities.
I pray to my precious glorious lama, lord of Dharma, who clears
away the darkness of ignorance.
In this verse we are acknowledging our tremendous gratitude towards
the lama, reminding ourselves that he teaches the supreme path to
liberation, that he displays to us all sublime qualities, since he is our
personal connection to the Buddhas, and that he clears away the darkness
of ignorance which prevents us from becoming enlightened.
Please bestow empowerment upon me!
Please bless me with the power to engage in the practice with
complete dedication!
We are now supplicating the lama to bestow empowerment upon us, which
is a formal ritual to connect us to his enlightened wisdom (as described in
the section which follows). In Mahayana -Buddhism the empty nature
of mind is presented through philosophical and contemplative analysis,
so the mind ‘solves' emptiness and discovers it. Through empowerment
(abeshika in Sanskrit), not only the mind but body, speech and mind are
introduced as a manifestation of our Buddha-nature, as if to say 'you
have that!' We are not receiving something external, but rather we are
activating recognition of something within ourselves.
We also pray to the lama to empower us so we can engage in (Dharma)
practice with complete dedication. This request is a powerful way to
create conditions which are conducive to authentic Dharma practice.
May all obstacles clear so I may dedicate my life to the practice!
May I experience the essence of the practice!
255
.



-
--
BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
Obstacles to spiritual practice include external obstacles such as traffic
fines or adversaries acting against us, and internal obstacles such
as thoughts of miserliness or lust which steal our minds away from
Dharma practice. We also pray to experience the essence of the practice,
which means attaining true realisation rather than just intellectual
understanding.
May my dedication and focus be flawless!
May I naturally emanate love, compassion and bodhicitta!
To ensure our Dharma practice is successful we need dedication or
devotion to the Dharma, good focus or single-pointed concentration, and
the ability to cultivate love, compassion and bodhicitta, which should
become such a part of us that we naturally emanate these qualities.
May I unite perfect concentration and insight!
May I attain true experience and supreme realisation
of the Dharma!
We can experience the truth of our Buddha-nature and completely
eradicate our mental defilements if we are able to unite perfect
concentration and insight. We therefore pray that we will attain
shamatha, the state of perfect single-pointed concentration by which the
mind can be powerfully focused like a spotlight upon any object we
choose, and that this will lead to vipasyaņa, the state of clear insight into
the true nature of reality42.
May I perfect the practice of the profound vajrayoga path!
Finally, we pray to the lama that we may be able to practise and
accomplish the profound path of vajrayoga, which is the extraordinary
tantric method of the Jonang Kalachakra tradition known as the Six
Vajra Yogas (to be explained in a later section).
42 Shamatha is both a method of meditation (also known as calm-abiding or
single-pointed meditation) and an advanced stage of perfect undistracted attention.
Vipasyana (also known as clear seeing or insight meditation) refers to meditation
on the empty nature of deceptive reality. These two forms of meditation as well as
the stages to accomplish them, are described in detail in chapter 5 of Unveiling Your
Sacred Truth: Meditation - How to Make the Mind Calm, Clear and Strong.

(iv) Receiving the Four Empowerments
From the OM at the forehead of my root lama, the great
Vajradhara,
Light streams forth and dissolves into my forehead chakra, purifying
obscurations of the body.
May I receive the vase empowerment and be blessed by the
enlightened body!
Through the four empowerments we are introduced to the holy body,
speech, mind and primordial wisdom of the lama, which are in fact a
manifestation of our own Buddha-nature. The body, speech and mind'
we are being introduced to have many different levels of meaning, but in
a simple way we are purifying the subtle body (made up of channels and
chakras), the subtle speech (or inner wind), the subtle mind (or essences)
and finally the residue of all three combined (known as the alaya or
storehouse consciousness)43. According to the Kalachakra system, the
true four empowerments take place with a secret wisdom consort and
the practice of receiving the empowerments here represents this more
profound level44
With the first empowerment, also known as the vase empowerment, white
light radiates from the lama's forehead and dissolves into your forehead
chakra, located at the mid-pont between the eyes about a centimetre
above the nasal bridge. This purifies obscurations of the body, related to
negative actions such as stealing or inflicting physical harm on others,
and dismantles the defilements of the channels and chakras. You are
therefore blessed by the (enlightened) vajra body, become a receptive
vessel for visualisation practice and have the seeds for attaining the
nirmanakaya planted within you.
From the AH at my lama's throat,
Light streams forth and dissolves into my throat chakra,
43 For a detailed explanation of the make-up of the subtle body, see chapter 20
ofUnveiling Your Sacred Truth: The Unique Kalachakra Tantric Meditation
44 More details of the hidden or secret meaning of these four empowerments,
and how they correspond to particular practices of the Six Vajra Yogas, can be found in
chapter 18 of Unveiling Your Sacred Truth.
257



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
purifying obscurations of speech.
May I receive the secret empowerment and be
blessed by the enlightened speech!
With the second empowerment, known as the secret empowerment,
red light radiates from the lama's throat and dissolves into your throat
chakra, located just above the Adam's apple. This purifies obscurations
of the speech, related to negative actions of speech such as speaking
harshly or untruthfully, and dismantles the defilements of the inner wind.
You are therefore blessed by the enlightened (vajra) speech, become a
receptive vessel for mantra recitation practice and have the seeds for
attaining the sambhogakaya planted within you.
From the HUM at my lama's heart,
Light streams forth and dissolves into my heart chakra,
purifying obscurations of mind.
May I receive the wisdom empowerment and
be blessed by the enlightened mind!
With the third empowerment, also known as the wisdom empowerment,
blue light radiates from the lama's heart and dissolves into your heart
chakra. This purifies obscurations of the mind, related to thoughts such
as greed, hatred and fixed views, and dismantles the defilements of the
subtle 'essences. You are therefore blessed by the enlightened (vajra)
mind, become a receptive vessel for practices such as tummo (involving
the subtle winds and channels) and have the seeds for attaining the
dharmakaya planted within you.
From the HO at my lama's navel,
Light streams forth and dissolves into my navel chakra, purifying all
propensities of conceptual thought and attachment.
May I attain the sacred fourth empowerment;
May I be imprinted with the four Buddha-kayas and blessed by the
indestructible primordial wisdom!
With the fourth empowerment, known as the sacred fourth (or word)
empowerment, yellow light radiates from the lama's navel and dissolves
into your navel chakra, which is actually located about four finger-widths
below the navel. This purifies all propensities of conceptual thought
and attachment, which refers to the cognitive obscurations and karmic
imprints stored in alaya, the storehouse consciousness or “ground of all’.
This dismantles the defilements which are left as a residue of the three
258



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
types of defilements already mentioned. You are therefore blessed by the
indestructible (vajra) primordial wisdom, become a receptive vessel for
direct meditation on the ultimate truth and have the seeds for attaining
the svabhavikakaya planted within you.
The lama melts into light and dissolves into me.
My own mind becomes inseparable with the dharmakaya mind of
the lama.
May I remain effortlessly in this non-conceptual unfabricated
state...
[Try to remain in this state beyond all ordinary concepts for as long as you can)
As in the preceding practices, you end the guru yoga practice by
dissolving the entire visualisation and watching the inseparability of
you and the lama. The lama therefore melts into light and dissolves into
you, and as this is happening your mind becomes inseparable with the
dharmakaya mind of the lama. When you begin the practice, dualism
still exists in the mind; like mixing rice with barley, the two are clearly
distinguishable from one another. Later on there is no notion of being
separate at all and your mind becomes completely mixed with the
wisdom mind of the lama, like pouring milk into water - once combined
you cannot identify one from the other. Finally you come to realise that
there was never any separation between you and the lama, which is none
other than your own Buddha-nature. You are not only mixing your mind,
but the entire dimension of your being including body and speech.
After mingling your mind with the lama's wisdom mind you should
remain effortlessly in this non-conceptual unfabricated state as best as
you can, with your mind mixed with the mind of the lama for as long as
you can sustain this. Once you lose this sense of oneness, you can then
recite prayers for a few minutes and then experience the lama dissolving
into you once again, just watching this without any preconceived ideas.
It may take a while to understand or get the hang of this practice, and
we should not complain if nothing happens right away. In order for it
to work many conditions must be present on the part of the giver, the
receiver and the connection. The lama has to be purely connected to an
authentic lineage, we need a great deal of merit to generate and sustain
the right kind of devotion, and we need a good relationship or close
karmic connection with the lama.
259



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
(v) Dedication
May I become just like you, glorious root and lineage lamas.
May my followers, life-span, noble title and pure realm become just
like yours!
We dedicate the virtue of this guru yoga practice by aspiring to emulate
the glorious root and lineage lamas. It is our limited perception that
prevents us from seeing the truth that these lamas are in fact fully
enlightened Buddhas, and we should aspire to follow their example so
we can uncover our own Buddha-nature.
In the second line, we are aspiring to attain all the enlightened qualities
of our lama. This includes an entourage of followers around us that we
have the power to control in an enlightened way in order to achieve
our enlightened purpose. This is a result of our merit. Life-span refers
to a long-life so that we may benefit beings in the best possible way.
Noble title refers to how we manifest for other's benefit, whether this
be as a Shambala Rigden King, a simple monk or a wandering hermit.
Finally, pure realm refers to the manifestation of the merit the lama has
accumulated while on the path to Buddhahood, just as Buddha Amitabha
dedicated oceans of merit so that beings may be reborn in his pure realm
if they remembered his name at the moment of their death.
Through the power of my prayers to you,
May all disease, poverty and conflict be pacified!
May the precious Dharma and everything auspicious increase
throughout the universe!
With this verse we dedicate the virtue of the practice so that all disease,
poverty and conflict are pacified throughout the world and that everything
that is virtuous and auspicious, especially the precious Dharma, will
increase throughout the universe and lead all beings to the ultimate
happiness of enlightenment.

HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
FAX.
PART THREE: Unique Kalachakra
Preliminary & Main Practices
II.1.4-
I. Innate Kalachakra Practice
Introduction
In the innate Kalachakra practice we visualise ourselves in the enlightened
form of the two-armed Kalachakra deity, known as Dukor Lhangkye45.
This is the first of the two unique preliminaries for the Six Vajra Yogas
according to the Jonang tradition, and is also known as the generation
stage in highest yoga-tantra46. We can engage in this practice if we have
received any highest yoga-tantra empowerment, though it is better to
have received the Kalachakra initiation. This is essential, however, if we
wish to practise the Six Yogas completion stage.
When you ‘generate yourself' as an enlightened deity, you are not
generating a fabricated, make-believe reality. Instead you are using an
extraordinary skilful method to bring you closer to the non-dual reality
of enlightenment. With this method you can view the universe as pure
and all beings in it as enlightened, even though they have all sorts of
defilements to overcome on a relative level. You can therefore embrace
reality with a much clearer, compassionate and vaster view.
Currently we are stuck in all sorts of dualistic notions, distinctions
and negative emotions. Meditating upon oneself as a deity helps you
45 Self-generation as the two-armed Innate Kalachakra, as used in the Jonang
tradition, differs from the visualisations used in other traditions which have, for
example, sixteen arms and place greater emphasis on the many intricate details of the
Kalachakra mandala. This practice is described in extensive detail in chapters. 19 of
Unveiling Your Sacred Truth: Generation of the Kalachakra Universe.
46 While this generation practice is the first unique preliminary for the Six
Vajra Yogas, the second is a dark room tantric meditation practice. This practice is
described in extensive detail in chapter 20 of Unveiling Your Sacred Truth.
261



-
-
BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
dismantle this cocoon of delusion by introducing you to a pure Buddha-
realm which is free from all dualistic limitations. It therefore allows you
to transform all impure experiences into pure perception until you realise
that everything has been pure all along. Although this pure perception
is not yet the actual experience of emptiness, you are coming closer
and closer to it. Therefore pure perception is used as a thorn to take out
another bigger thorn in your palm. Once you are thoroughly familiar
with the nature of this smaller thorn, you are then qualified to practise
the completion stage, where you meditate directly on emptiness.

As with any Mahayana practice, you should make sure that you have
taken refuge and cultivated the supreme intention of bodhicitta. You
then begin the practice, first by establishing the visualisation and then
reciting the mantra. This visualisation practice should contain three key
features: presence, clarity and purity of perception. Presence, or divine
262



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
---
-
S
.
-
.
-
pride, is to do with the strength of feeling or emotional connection you
have with the visualisation. Clarity is the awareness of details which is
gradually imprinted in our minds through practice, which are vibrant
and translucent like a rainbow, not rigid and concrete. Pure perception is
when you realise the true significance of the symbols that you visualise.
If you are overwhelmed by all the details, remember that the feeling of
presence and confidence is what is most important.
The Kalachakra Generation Practice with Commentary
(i) Visualisation
[Having first established the mind of refuge and bodhicitta, recite]:
OM SHUNYATA JNANA VAJRA SVABHAVA ATMAKO HAM
Reciting this mantra, quickly visualise yourself and all phenomena
dissolving into the natural state beyond concepts and remain in this
state for a while. You should think with absolute confidence, 'I am the
primordial natural state of reality, beyond subject and object”. Try to
dwell in this non-conceptual state as best you can.
Arising from emptiness, I instantly and spontaneously appear as Innate
Kalachakra.
I appear upon a seat formed by a lotus, moon, sun, rahu and
kalagni,
Which lies upon the summit of Mount Meru and the universe of four
elements.
My body is blue in colour, with one face, two arms and three eyes.
I embrace the consort Vishvamati and I hold a vajra and bell at my
chest.
From the empty state beyond concepts, you are infused with the intention
of bodhicitta and instantly appear as Innate Kalachakra, known as Dukor
Lhangkye in Tibetan. Within the enlightened mind of innate Kalachakra
appears a series of four concentric discs (as depicted in the mandala
offering section) representing the universe of the four elements: (from
"
263



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
-- ILLA SAAR-
the bottom) a vast wind mandala, a fire mandala, a water mandala and an
earth mandala. In the centre of the earth mandala appears Mount Meru47,
on top of which appears a multicoloured lotus flower and then a moon
disc, sun disc, black rahu disc and yellow kalagni disc48. The moon disc
symbolises bodhicitta, the sun disc the realisation of emptiness, the rahu
disc immutable bliss and the kalagni disc the empty form.
Kalachakra stands majestically upon this seat. He is blue in colour,
symbolising the ultimate purity of the central channel, and he has one
face symbolising the one ultimate natural truth of all phenomena. His
two arms symbolise the method and wisdom of the primordial state
or the inseparability of immutable great bliss and empty form, and his
three eyes symbolise direct perception of the past, present and future.
He embraces the consort Vishvamati with hands stretched out holding
a vajra in the right hand and a bell in the left, symbolising the ultimate
unity of method and wisdom or the masculine and feminine aspects of
enlightenment.
Kalachakra's neck has three colours - black in the middle, red on the
right side and white on the left side, white symbolising the elimination
of atoms, darkness and courage (the Kalachakra equivalent of ignorance,
attachment and aversion). The words atoms, darkness and courage are
the language used by the highest Hindu Samkhya belief system, and are
used here as a skilful method to lead those familiar with this belief to a
correct path.
My white left leg is drawn in and tramples the heart of the white
creation god.
My red right leg is extended and tramples the heart of the red desire
god.
My head is adorned with a top-knot of plaited locks, a wish-fulfilling
jewel and a crescent moon.
47 A detailed description of Mt Meru appears in chapter 17 of Unveiling Your
Sacred Truth: The Sublime Universal Mandala Offering, and also in the mandala
offering section of the current text.
48 The rahu and kalagni represent solar and lunar eclipses – their meaning is
explained in greater detail in the mandala offering section.

BERSIG-
Kalachakra has two legs and is standing on top of two samsaric gods
linked to the Hindu tradition,
symbolising freedom from samsara and nirvana. The white left leg is
slightly bent and crushes the chest of a wrathful one-faced, three-eyed
white creation god who wears a tiger skin and snake ornament and is
lying face up, having fainted. This signifies the transformation of the left
main channel lalana and elimination of the four afflictions (attachment,
aversion, ignorance and ego). The red right leg is standing straight and
crushing the chest of the red desire god who has a peaceful face, two
arms and wears jewelled ornaments, again lying face up having fainted.
This signifies the transformation of the right main channel rasana and
the elimination of the four maras (the aggregates, affliction, death and
pleasurable objects). The white creation god is also known as Ishvara
while the red desire god is known as Karmadeva.
Kalachakra's head is adorned with a top-knot of thick hair plaited into
locks which hangs loosely down his back, and on top of this is a precious
wish-fulfilling jewel draped in silk and flowing downward. In front of the
top knot is a multi-coloured crossed vajra symbolising the four sublime
powers of a Buddha - pacifying, increasing, controlling and wrathfully
subduing. Above the vajra is a crescent moon symbolising immutable
bliss.
IL
I am wearing vajra ornaments and a lower garment of tiger skin.
My fingers are of five different colours and the three sections of each
finger are also of different colours.
Vajrasattva is seated upon the crown of my head,
And I stand in the centre of a burning ring of flames of five different
colours.
My facial expression shows a mixture of wrath and passion.
Kalachakra is adorned with numerous vajra ornaments made of
indestructible diamonds such as earrings, necklaces, armlets, belt, anklets
and malas. He is draped in silk scarves, symbolising the indestructible
immutable bliss of the enlightened mind, and is wearing a lower garment
of tiger skin symbolising the elimination of pride and arrogance.
The five digits of the left and right hand are of five different colours -
the thumb is yellow, the index finger is white, the middle finger is red,
the ring finger is black and the fifth finger is green. These symbolise the
265



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
purification of five aspects of lalana (the left main channel) which result
in the attainment of the five wisdoms – the all-encompassing wisdom,
mirror-like wisdom, wisdom of equanimity, wisdom of discrimination
and the all-accomplishing wisdom. The three sections of each finger49
are of three different colours - the first (nearest the tip) is black, the
middle section is red and the section closest to the hand is white. These
colours symbolise the purification of sarana (the right main channel) and
the attainment of the indestructible vajra body, speech and mind. The
crown is adorned with a blue-coloured Vajrasattva, symbolising that
Kalachakra primarily belongs to the Vajrasattva Buddha-family.
Luminous rays of light of five different colours radiate outwards to the
ring of flames a body's length away from Kalchakra's body, and both the
light and fire extend outwards still further. The face has an appearance
of wrath and power, with the top incisors extending over the bottom lip,
and the three eyes are rounded and slightly bloodshot. The expression
shows a mixture of uncompromising wrathful energy and passionate
love or divine sexual energy. This signifies indestructible compassion
and immutable bliss.
My consort Vishvamati has a body yellow in colour, with one face,
two arms and three eyes.
She holds a curved knife in her right hand and a skull cup in her left
hand.
With her right leg drawn in and her left leg extended, we are standing
together in union.
She is naked and adorned with the five bone ornaments.
Half of her hair is tied in a top-knot and the rest is falling loose.
Kalachakra is embracing the consort Vishvamata, and they are both
inseparably in union (known as Kalachakra Yab-yum). The Vishamata
aspect has a golden yellow body, one face, two arms, three eyes, and she
is holding a curve-bladed skinning knife (tikug) in her right hand which
is embracing Kalachakra. She holds a skull cup in her left hand, offering
divine nectar to Kalachakra. Her right leg is drawn in and wrapped
around Kalachakra and her left leg is extended, as she stands together
with Kalachakra in divine sexual union. She is naked and adorned with
a golden wheel on her crown and five bone ornaments - bone earrings,
49 These three longitudinal sections represent an “inner aspect of each finger,
as the outside of each finger has only one particular colour.

HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
armlets, bracelets, anklets, belt and necklaces. Half of her hair is tied in
a top-knot at her crown and half is flowing down her back, symbolising
how all phenomena ultimately have a nature of empty form.
At my forehead is the syllable OM
At the throat is AH
At the heart is HUM
At the navel is HO
At the secret place is SVA
At the crown is HA
Both deities have a white-coloured OM at their forehead, representing
the pure nature of the water element and Amitabha, the body of all the
Buddhas. At their throat is a red AH syllable representing the pure nature
of the fire element and Ratnasambhava, the speech of all the Buddhas.
At their heart is a black HUM syllable representing the pure nature of
the air element and Amoghasiddhi, the mind of all the Buddhas. At
their navel is a yellow HO, representing the pure nature of the earth
element and Vairochana, the indestructible wisdom of all the Buddhas.
At their secret place is a blue SVA syllable, representing the pure nature
of the primordial mind element and Vajrasattva, the ultimate purity of
the Buddhas' primordial mind. Finally, upon their crown is a green HA
syllable representing the pure nature of the space element and Akshobya,
the activity of all the Buddhas.
The purpose of visualising the six syllables is not just to bless or
transform these particular locations on your body, but to understand that
Kalachakra and Vishvamata are the pure embodiment of the six realms
of samsara50 and that this is no different to your own primordial nature.
Light-rays emanate outwards from my heart and the entire universe
becomes a Buddha-field,
Inhabited by innumerable mandalas of deities.
Next, rays of luminous light of six different colours emanate outwards
from Kalachakra's heart and the six syllables, reaching out to the six
realms of samsara. The Buddha-field of the Kalachakra Mandala
pervades the entire universe of the six realms, and the light transforms
all beings into innumerable mandalas of enlightened dieties.
50 The six realms of samsara include the human and animal realms, as well as
various unseen realms such as the god, demi-god, hungry ghost and hell realms.
267



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
With confidence, remind yourselfthat you are Kalachakra and Vishvamata
in union and make your visualisation clear, vibrant and translucent as
rainbow light, unlike an ordinary picture or statue. Remain in this state
of natural Kalachakra for as long as you wish.
(ii) Mantra Recitation & Dissolution
[You can keep the mind focused single-pointedly upon this visualisation for as long
as you wish. Then recite the mantra while visualising the mantra symbol]:
OM HAKSHA MALA VARAYA (SVAHA)
Having stabilised the visualisation of Innate Kalachakra, you should
then visualise the Kalachakra mantra symbol at your heart and recite
the mantra. The best way to recite the mantra is to bring to mind an
understanding of the many different levels of meaning of each syllable
(as described below or in chapter 19 of Sacred Truth), while also holding
a clear visualisation in your mind. It may be recited aloud or silently,
though either way there must be a distinct sound for each syllable. The
best method is to recite the mantra with a whisper, ensuring this is not
too loud.
To visualise the mantra symbol (sometimes known as the ten-fold
powerful one), visualise a lotus at your heart with layered discs upon
it - a moon disc, sun disc, rahu disc and kalagni disc. On top of these
discs appears the mantra symbol with interconnected coloured letters,
as shown above. From the top downwards, there is a blue HA, a green
KSHA, a multi-coloured MA, a yellow LA, a white VA, a red RA and a
black YA51.
At the top is a white crescent moon with a red sun on it and a dark purple
nadu (like a small flame) arising from the sun.
51 For more extensive details on the form of the mantra and its symbolism see
chapter 19 of Unveiling Your Sacred Truth.
268



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
The mantra syllables have multiple levels ofmeaning, symbolising various
aspects of the inner Kalachakra (the subtle body), the outer Kalachakra
(the external universe) and the other Kalachakra (the Kalachakra path to
enlightenment). In a general sense it signifies the entire Buddha-dharma,
including the three vehicles and 84,000 teachings of the Buddha52. It also
represents the six elements which make up all conventional phenomena
and are the main objects of purification – wind (YA), fire (RA), water
(VA), earth (LA), consciousness (MA), and space (HA). These elements
are also associated with six aspects of
the path to enlightenment and the six
Buddha-families, the final result of
enlightenment. In addition, the green
KSHA represents the primordial mind
element, the crescent moon represents
the white essence and left main channel,
the sun represents the red essence and
the right main channel and the nadu
represents the central channel.

created, including the environment and deities of the entire mandala. First
