from the periphery to the centre, leaving the inner mantra symbol in
the centre of his chest. Next the mantra symbol dissolves from the base
upwards to the nadu. The nadu at the top of this symbol then gradually
disappears into emptiness and you remain in this open state of awareness
for as long as you can.
In this way the entire visualisation dissolves and merges with your being
like water being poured into water. Throughout the practice you should
have a clear understanding that Kalachakra and Vishvamata in embrace
is in fact you, and when you dissolve this you should simply watch this
inseparability.
(iii) Dedication
By the power of this virtue,
May I swiftly attain the state of Kalachakra,
And lead all beings to Kalachakra enlightenment!
As with the preceding practices, you end by dedicating the merit so that
you will swiftly attain the state of Kalachakra through the practice of
the Six Vajra Yogas. Your aim should be to lead all beings to the state
of Kalachakra enlightenment, at which time the rupakaya form body
of enlightenment will spontaneously bring benefit to countless sentient
beings.
[This text, “The Divine Ladder – 'The Preliminary & Main Practices of
the Profound Kalachakra Vajrayoga', was composed by Drolway Gonpo
(Taranatha). It describes how the great Jonangpa tantric lineage masters
and their heart-sons practised, and includes the essence of all the pure
lineage instructions).
The author of this text is Taranatha, the great 17th century Jonang master
who was both a brilliant scholar and highly realised practitioner. It
gathers together the essential instructions which were passed on from
one generation of lineage masters to the next, from the tantric lineage
masters to their heart-sons. The great practitioners of the past practiced
in this way, and we should consider it a tremendous blessing to be able
to follow in their footsteps.

II. Wensum: Three isolations( Tantric
Shtamatha
As discussed, Kalachakra tantra requires completion of 5 common
and 2 uncommon preliminary practices. The last of the 2 uncommon
preliminary practices is known in Tibetan as wensum. This advanced
practice is not stated in the root text as it is traditionally transmitted
directly from the tantric teacher to the student.
While wensum is more comprehensive than this brief interpretation,
students who do not have a teacher should find the overview of great
benefit to their Kalachakra practice.
The body according to tantra
According to many tantras, the body consists of a dynamic subtle
network of channels, inner winds and subtle essences. This is not
considered objectively real but an experience had by meditators. For
the purpose of this explanation, the student should know:
-
the central channel
runs as a straight line from the crown of the head to the head
of the perineum
two types of winds
root and secondary
Both root and secondary winds have the capacity to transform an
ordinary mind into an enlightened mind with correct practice.
Root winds
Digestion
Excretion
Swallowing
Movement
271



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
Sustaining of life
Secondary winds
Flow
Flowing well
Flowing very well
Strong flow
Certain flow
The Practice
Length
wensum practice is generally 2 hours in length, 4 times a day (when on
retreat), otherwise once a day is sufficient.
.5 hours
Posture and foundations
1.5 hours
Meditation as described
Environment
A completely dark room which light cannot enter at all (you must not
even be able to see yourself). If this is not possible, you can use a cover
or mask that enables you to open your eyes into complete darkness (no
light at all).
Posture
The seven aspect posture is primary to practice:
1) Legs crossed in the full lotus position, right foot resting on the
left thigh and left foot resting against the right thigh
2) Back straight like an arrow
3) Neck straight with the head slightly tilted forward
4) Thumbs pressed into the base of the ring finger and hands
closed tightly (make a fist)
272



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
5) Arms taut and straight with locked hands pressed into the groin
with upper body extended (in the beginning you can make a
modification here)
6) Mouth and teeth relaxed with the tip of the tongue touching the
gum behind the top teeth
7) Eyes wide open gazing about twelve inches from the forehead
into darkness
Foundation
Briefly go through the practices of refuge, bodhicitta, Vajrasattva
purification, mandala offering and guru yoga.
Kalachakra foundation
As in the Kalachakra practice, visualise yourself as Kalachakra and
generate great joy and enthusiasm that you have the opportunity to
train your body, speech and mind.
Wensum: Three isolations (also called distractions)
Non-distraction of body
Through the force of meditation upon particular points in the body
created by the seven point posture, winds enter and dissolve into the
central channel and we naturally experience the enlightened mind as
winds flow freely here. Without the ability to direct the inner winds
through the central channel there will be no chance of attaining
the non-conceptual primordial mind or accomplishment of the Six
Kalachakra Yogas.
The main sign or achievement of the non-distraction of body is the
ability to perform the posture without any discomfort or difficulty
for as long as we desire, although at times a little fatigue may be
experienced.
Non-distraction of speech
If we are caught up in or attached to ordinary daily speech our inner
wind dissipates through the minor channels (rasana and lalana) and no
longer remains within the central channel.
273.:



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
As soon as the seven essential physical points have been assumed:
-
forcefully blow out stale breath nine times through the nose,
beginning with three breaths through the left nostril, then
three breaths through the right nostril and finally three breaths
through both nostrils. This enables you to release the afflicted
inner winds and clear the channels
-
after that, leave the breath alone and allow it to move naturally
The main sign or achievement of the non-distraction of speech is the
ability to stay silent for as long as we like, without experiencing any
hardship or boredom.
Non-distraction of mind
If we are caught up in or attached to ordinary dualistic thoughts it is
impossible to control and direct the inner winds through the central
channel, as thoughts and the inner winds are interdependent.
The essential point for training the mind is to remain in a natural state:
-
do not think of anything in particular and do not exert effort to
make your mind tighter or looser
try not to concentrate or relax or look intensely out into space,
nor inwards toward oneself
-
do not rely upon anything
remain at ease and without fabrication in regard to whatever
arises
In time the student will develop through four stages:
Perceiving
At this stage the mind has greater awareness
yet it cannot remain in single-pointed focus
for long
Habituation
274



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
As thoughts arise they spontaneously vanish,
enabling the student to remain in single-
pointed focus without effort
Stabilisation
By continuing to practise, thoughts hardly
arise at all, your mind is not disturbed and
does not lose concentration. Thoughts now
arise and then gently pass away.
Perfection stabilisation
The mind becomes so skilled you can
choose whether to have a still mind which
is spontaneously single-pointed, or to focus
without distraction on a topic of analysis
The main sign of the non-distraction of mind is that our mind finally
becomes subdued, clear, aware and bright, and it can be used as
directed without any problems.
Between sessions
Between sessions you do not necessarily have to remain in the dark
room. However, it is crucial to try and maintain a state of clear lucid
awareness and refrain from engaging in meaningless conversation. In
retreat it is usual to have three light meals each day.
When we are able to naturally focus with the mind of shamatha, you
will experience ten signs or visual apparitions: smoke, mirage, clouds,
fireflies, sunlight, moonlight, blazing gemstones, eclipse, starlight and
rays of light. These are merely the appearance of the enlightened mind,
not the enlightened mind itself. However, these signs are not illusion;
they are the truth of empty form, which then become the basis for the
more advanced practices of the Six Kalachakra Yogas.
275



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
Aspiration Prayer to Accomplish
the Six Vajra Yogas
What follows is a prayer to accomplish the Six Vajra Yogas, the main
practice in the Jonang tradition54. These are very advanced practices and
a strong foundation in the preliminaries is required before commencing
them, including the six preliminaries described here as well as a single-
pointed meditation practice carried out in a dark room, known as the
three isolationsss.
By practising the Six Vajra Yogas you develop the ability to see yourself
and your environment in terms of empty form, based on the perception
of ten signs that appear during the initial dark room practice56. Through
special yogic techniques, this perception of empty form is mixed with the
mind and inner wind, and this is made to enter into the central channel
and dissolve the subtle essences located at the six chakra centres. As a
result of this practice the material body and inner winds are gradually
exhausted and eventually disappear, so that one attains an illusory
rainbow body at the point of enlightenment.
There is no specific root text for the practice of the Six Vajra Yogas,
and instructions for this profound practice can only be obtained from a
qualified Kalachakra lineage holder. As it is quite an advanced practice,
you must practise on an aspiration level until you are able to control the
channels, chakras and inner winds or until your Dharma teacher believes
you are qualified to begin the practice.
OM AH HUM HO HANGKYA.
54 The Six Vajra Yogas are described in greater detail in chapter 23 of
Unveiling Your Sacred Truth: The Tantric Path to Liberation. Complete instructions
for the practices, however, can only be obtained from a lama who holds an authentic
Kalachakra lineage.
55 The practice of the three isolations involves meditating with eyes wide open
in a completely dark room with a special posture.
56 These ten signs include: smoke, mirage, clouds, fire-flies, sunlight,
moonlight, blazing gemstones, eclipse, starlight, rays of light.

HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
Through the power of Buddha-nature,
May I cut the conceptual movement of my mind.
May I experience the ten signs and clear-light mind,
And attain the path of withdrawal yoga.
I pray to my saviours, my kind lama and the heirs of the holy
lineage.
Bless me so that this is accomplished!
The six syllable mantra at the beginning of this verse independently
symbolizes both the six chakras and the six yoga practices. The power of
Buddha-rature refers to the ‘Tathagathagharba', the primordial ground
or natural Buddha residing in the continuum of every being, through
which all enlightened qualities are obtained.
The next three lines describe the first of the Six Vajra Yogas, known as
withdrawal. This includes a night time practice, carried out in a dark room
with eyes wide open, and a day-time practice which involves focusing
one's vision on the clear blue sky. Through these practices the conceptual
movement of my mind is cut as the ten inner winds which circulate the
subtle body are absorbed into the central channel, and the ten signs and
clear-light mind are experienced, which then become stronger, clearer
and more stable. Six of these signs are objects of the day time practice
while the remaining four are objects of the night time practice. Through
practice an 'inner world' is built up on the basis of these ten signs, which
is quite independent of the outside world. These signs, however, are still
conceived as objects which are separate from the mind.
Finally, as this is an aspiration prayer you pray to the kind lama and all
the heirs of the holy lineage, as the practice can only be accomplished
with a connection to the transmission lineage and devotion towards the
lama.
Through the power of Buddha-nature,
May my speech, inner wind and consciousness become
unwavering.
May my wisdom increase, along with the joy and bliss of analysis,
And may I attain the path of stabilisation yoga.
I pray to my saviours, my kind lama and the heirs of the holy
lineage.
Bless me so that this is accomplished!
277



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
Si=
.
This verse refers to the second of the Six Vajra Yogas, known as
meditative stabilisation or great concentration. Through this yoga, the
perception of empty forms attained in the previous practice is unified
indivisibly with the awareness of an inner perceiver, and therefore one's
speech, inner wind and consciousness become unwavering. While the
first yoga allows one to perceive the empty forms of the ten signs as the
objects of the mind, the second yoga enables the practitioner to “mix'
these signs with the mind and experience the joy and bliss of analysis.
Prior to this stage, you only practise with the eye sense and visual forms.
Now, however, you practise with each of the sense consciousnesses and
their objects individually, including sound, smell, taste and touch - and
special conditions such as a dark room are not necessarily needed.

lineage.
Bless me so that this is accomplished!.
The third of the Six Vajra Yogas is known as harnessing the life-force or
life-force yoga. Previously the empty forms have been mixed with the
mind itself; and now the empty forms and mind become mixed with the
inner winds so there is no separation between these three entities. The ten
winds of lalana and rasana, the left and right main channels, are unified
as they are drawn into the central channel avadhuti, and the circulation
of the inner wind in the left and right channels thereby ceases. This is
achieved by focusing on the navel centre where the blazing fire of tummo
is experienced, often known as “inner heat practice as physical heat is
generated by this process. In addition, the energy in the central channel
rises to the crown and melts the visualised syllable HAM, and bliss can
be felt as the energy descends from one chakra to the next.
Through the power of Buddha-nature,
May the white essence be retained and stabilised at my forehead.
May I experience unchanging bliss as the essences melt,
And attain the path of retention yoga.
I pray to my saviours, my kind lama and the heirs of the holy
lineage.
Bless me so that this is accomplished!
This verse refers to the fourth yoga, known as retention. During the
278



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
previous stage the practitioner is able to retain the essential bodily
fluids and thereby unify empty forms, winds and awareness. Through
this yoga these three elements are then integrated with the indestructible
subtle fluid essences located in the six subtle chakra centers. This is
achieved by working on the gross bodily fluids (sperm, lymph and
blood) in order to control the subtle fluid essences using four tantric
consorts - the visualised consort, physical consort, dakini consort and
great empty form consort. Through this practice the white essence is
retained and stabilised at the forehead and immutable or unchanging
bliss is experienced as the subtle fluid essences melt. The white essence
is a subtle 'seed' that comes from the father's semen and gives birth to
'white' tissue such as bones, marrow, brain and spinal cord.
Through the power of Buddha-nature,
May all my chakras, channels and petals be filled with the pure
essence of great bliss.
May I attain mastery of the three glorious consorts,
And attain the path of recollection yoga.
I pray to my saviours, my kind lama and the heirs of the holy
lineage.
Bless me so that this is accomplished!
1
The fifth of the Six Vajra Yogas is known as recollection, and at this
stage the integrated winds and essences are stabilised so that all the
chakras, channels and petals are filled with the pure essence of great
bliss. Through this arises mastery of the three glorious consorts within
the six chakras, and the essences are therefore perfectly contained. The
aim is to be supported by the great empty form consort alone (or consort
of infinite empty forms), which means supreme immutable bliss can be
experienced without relying at all on the other three consorts.
Through the power of Buddha-nature,
May the six chakras of my subtle body be filled with the white essence
of immutable great bliss.
May I experience the unshakeable non-dualistic mind
And attain the path of absorption yoga.
I pray to my saviours, my kind lama and the. heirs of the holy
lineage.
Bless me so that this is accomplished!
The final stage of the Six Vajra Yogas is meditative absorption. With the
fifth stage a stable absorption in the state of supreme immutable bliss is
279



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
achieved, and then during this stage one progresses along twelve further
stages of absorption. At the beginning of this stage the path of insight is
achieved, during which the unshakeable non-dualistic mind of emptiness
is experienced directly for the first time with perfect single-pointed
concentration. Now one attains an approximate Kalachakra form, similar
to the actual form of the enlightened deity, and an ever-increasing stream
of immutable bliss is experienced as the six chakras are filled with the
white essence of immutable great bliss and one progresses along the path
of habituation. There are 21,000 moments of immutable great bliss which
purify 21,000 defilements at each chakra, gradually dissolving the inner
winds and exhausting the elements of the material body. All afflictive
and cognitive obscurations are thereby eliminated and Buddhahood is
achieved in the form of the co-emergent Kalachakra deity.
Through the power of Buddha-nature,
May my body never be separated from the yogic postures,
May my mind never be separated from the profound pith instructions
of unmistaken Dharma,
And may I accomplish the path of the Six Vajra Yogas.
I pray to my saviours, my kind lama and the heirs of the holy
lineage.
Bless me so that this is accomplished!
This verse is a final aspiration prayer to accomplish the path of the Six
Vajra Yogas, as you pray that your body is never separated from the
(special) yogic postures and your mind is never separated from the
profound pith instructions which the lama gives you. In this context
pith instructions are the directions for the postures and profound yogic
meditation techniques which are transmitted orally by the lama rather
than being written down.
Dedication
Through this virtue,
May all beings abandon the meaningless concerns of samsara.
May they meditate upon the supremely meaningful vajrayoga path
And swiftly unveil the enlightenment of Kalachakra!
The Innate Kalachakra practice ends with a dedication prayer, wishing
that all beings abandon meaningless samsaric concerns and instead make
the most of the precious opportunity they have to attain enlightenment.
Specifically, you wish that they become connected with the supremely
280



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
---
-
meaningful vajrayoga path, as presented here in this text, and have the
ability to meditate upon the Six Vajra Yogas and so swiftly unveil the
enlightenment of Kalachakra.
Through this virtue,
May I swiftly attain the Six Vajra Yogas
And lead all beings without exception to the st ate of Kalachakra
enlightenment!
This second part of the dedication emphasises your personal wish to
attain the Six Vajra Yogas not only for your own sake but to lead all
beings without exception to the state of Kalachakra enlightenment. This
is also a reminder that the Six Vajra Yogas are a Mahayana practice,
through which you take personal responsibility to lead all beings to
enlightenment. This intention is what determines the result of your
practice.
Through this virtue,
May all beings complete the accumulation of merit and primordial
wisdom,
And so attain the two Buddha-kayas!
Finally, you dedicate the virtue so thatallbeings complete the accumulation
of merit and primordial wisdom, which are the cause for attaining the
dharmakaya truth body and rupakaya form body of enlightenment. The
form body is what spontaneously accomplishes the benefit of others, and
in this case it emerges in the form of the Kalachakra deity.

Introduction
In the Jonang tradition there are actually three separate guru yoga
practices – the foundation
guru yoga (described earlier
in this text), the Dolpopa
guru yoga and the Taranatha
guru yoga. These practices
offer a powerful method
to connect us with the holy
lineage, as Dolpopa and
Taranatha are considered to
be the two most influential
and extraordinary figures
in the Jonang Kalachakra
tradition.
Nowadays in Jonang
monasteries the guru yoga
practice is undertaken for a
maximum of three weeks. In
the first week this Dolpopa
Kunkyen Dolpopa
guru yoga is recited, in the second
week the Taranatha guru yoga is recited, and in the third week the
foundation guru yoga is practised. These profound practices are not just
preliminaries, as they also play a significant role in the practice of the
Six Vajra Yogas. Traditionally during a three year retreat the guru yoga
practices are performed every day in an alternating fashion, four times

each day57.
The Dolpopa guru yoga bears the title Guru Yoga - Rain of Blessings for
the Six Yogas of the Vajra Lineage. The practice can be considered a rain
of blessings as the recitations and prayers are designed to take us beyond
the ordinary mind by invoking the blessings of Dolpopa and the other
lineage masters. This opens the door to tantric realisation by giving us
the ability to authentically practice the Six Vajra Yogas as passed down
through this lineage.
The basic principles of this practice are the same as in the foundation
guru yoga, and these details are described earlier in this commentary.
The Dolpopa Guru Yoga Practice with Commentary
(i) Visualisation
Nama Shri Kalachakra.
I go for refuge with vivid faith in the lama, yidam
and the Three Jewels.
May I generate immeasurable love, compassion, joy
and equanimity towards all beings!
Nama is an expression of homage and Shri means glorious. Going
for refuge with vivid faith means our mind is clear and filled with joy,
gratitude and inspiration. This faith should also be eager and confident,
with complete trust in the lama, yidam and Three Jewels. You then
arouse the altruistic motivation of bodhicitta. by cultivating the four
immeasurables - immeasurable love, compassion, joy and equanimity -
and aspiring to attain complete enlightenment for their sake.
May I diligently practise the profound path of guru yoga for
the sake of all beings!
May all impure, temporary appearances dissolve into emptiness...
In the first line you arouse the motivation of bodhicitta, praying that you
will practise the profound path of guru yoga for the sake of all beings.
57 More details of the practice of guru yoga in the Jonang tradition can be
found in chapter 18 of Unveiling Your Sacred Truth: Guru Yoga - the Gateway to
Tantric Realisation.
283



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
Then you consider all impure, temporary appearances to dissolve into
the non-dual state, becoming like the reflection of the moon on a lake.
Seated on a throne on top of my crown,
Upon a five-layered seat of a lotus, moon disc and so forth,
My root lama appears as the great Vajradhara.
His body is blue in colour and has one face and two arms.
The practice begins by visualising your root lama in the form of
Vajradhara, as in the previous guru yoga, with a blue body, one face and
two arms. He abides above the crown of your head seated on a throne
which is supported by a five-layered seat consisting of a lotus, moon
disc, sun disc, black rahu disc and yellow kalagni disc. Each of these
layers has spiritual significance - the lotus signifies purity, the moon disc
symbolises compassion, the sun disc symbolises wisdom and the final
two discs represent the spiritual power of solar and lumar eclipses.
Although we are instructed to visualise Vajradhara, in this practice
it is more common to visualise your root lama to appear in the form
of Dolpopa. You may also choose, however, to visualise the form of
Vajradhara while recollecting the qualities of the omniscient Dolpopa.
As this practice was composed by Dolpopa it makes no mention of
using his form in the visualisation - this detail was added later to honour
Dolpopa's contribution to the lineage and connect with his spiritual
presence.
He is seated in full lotus position.
He is draped in elegant silk garments
And his body is adorned with precious jewels and bone ornaments.
He holds a vajra and bell crossed at his heart.
More details are given here about the visualised form of Vajradhara,
whose nature is your root lama. He is seated upon the throne in full
lotus posture and he wears silk garments, jewels and bone ornamaments,
which all symbolise particular aspects of enlightened reality. The vajra
and bell crossed at his heart symbolise the union of indestructible
wisdom and compassion.
The four centres of his body are marked with four syllables:
DZA HUM BAM HO
Light rays emanate outwards from the syllable HUM at his heart,
Invoking all the root and lineage lamas ,
Becoming inseparable with them.
The syllable DZA appears at the crown of Vajradhara's body. From the
284



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
HUM at the heart light rays stream forth in all directions and this light
becomes empowered by all the root and lineage lamas, so that you
become inseparable with their enlightened presence. In this way you
should visualise the body of Vajradhara dissolving into your own body.
(ii) Supplicating the Lama
Precious lama, I pay homage to your body, speech and mind.
Your body is adorned with unchanging, perfect marks and signs.
Your uninterrupted Brahma-like speech pervades the ten directions.
You abide in the unmistaken mind of the great seal.
With this verse you begin the supplication prayers to the lama by praising
the wonderful qualities of his body, speech and mind. The unchanging
marks and signs of his body refer, for example, to the 32 major marks
and 80 minor marks of a Buddha, and the uninterrupted Brahma-like
speech refers to the pleasing, beautiful and melodious speech of the
Brahma-like gods. The unmistaken mind of the great seal refers to the
unchanging qualitiy of the enlightened mind, which is like the king's
seal in that it cannot be altered. The great seal is also a reference to
Mahamudra, a direct method of meditation upon the non-dual state.
I prostrate to you who is the embodiment of
the thirty-six Tathagatas,
Unveiled as the six aggregates are purified.
This verse is the beginning of a seven-branch offering practice, in which
we prostrate or pay homage to the lama as the embodiment of the thirty-
six Tathagatas. This is a way of describing the result of enlightenment
according to the Kalachakra Tantra, with each of the six aggregates
becoming six male Tathagatas when fully purifieds. In addition, the
six elements become the six female Tathagatas, the six senses become
the six male bodhisattvas, the six sense objects become the six female
bodhisattvas, and the six action faculties and their corresponding actions 59
become the six: wrathful male and female deities.
58 These six aggregates include: form, feeling, perception, formation,
consciousness and primordial consciousness.
59 The six action faculties are: the mouth, arm/hand, legs, anus, urinary faculty
and regenerative faculty, while the six corresponding actions are: speaking, taking,
going, defaecating, urinating and emitting regenerative fluids.
285



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
Altogether there thus are 36 bases of purification which become the
thirty-six Tathagatas when purified.
I offer with joy and pure intention an inconceivable
ocean of Samantabhadra offerings,
Including all virtue of body, speech and mind gathered during
the three times!
This refers to the second part of the seven-branch offering, during which
you generate an inconceivable number of visualised offering objects to
the lama and Three Jewels, with the pure intention of wishing to liberate
all beings. This includes not only physical objects, but also virtue of
body, speech and mind gathered during the past, present and future.
Samantabhadra refers to the primordial Buddha who abides in the
limitless expanse of dharmakaya, and 'Samantabhadra offering' is a
way to describe the limitless nature of your offering. In the Kalachakra
tradition we also speak of twelve offering dakinis, and twelve further
offering dakinis arise from each of these. The offerings keep on
multiplying in this way until they become limitless.
I openly confess all my negativities amassed through body,
speech and mind,
And pray that they be purified.
I rejoice in all virtue!
I wholeheartedly request that you turn the wheel
of Dharma without ceasing!
I implore you to remain forever in samsara for
the sake of all beings!
The seven-branch offering continues as you confess all negativities
accumulated through harmful actions of body, speech and mind and pray
that they are all purified, with strong resolve not to repeat these actions
in the future. Although the lama's compassion is infinite, he will only
teach if we sincerely request that he turn the wheel of Dharma. Although
in reality the lama is beyond life and death, we implore him to remain
forever in samsara without passing into paranirvana for the sake of all
beings.
I pray to my glorious lama.
Your nature is inseparable from the four Buddha-kayas.
286



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
You are the chief of all vajra holders,
Having completed the three accumulations and attained
the twelve paths.
Please bless me!
As the lama is the embodiment of all the Buddhas, his nature is
inseparable with the three Buddha-kayas – the dharmakaya truth body,
the sambhogakaya enjoyment body and the nirmanakaya emanation
body. As he is the embodiment of all the masters who transmit the
profound tantric teachings, he is the chief of all vajra holders. The three
accumulations refer to generosity, great concentration and wisdom, while
the twelve paths refer to specific stages of attainment on the Kalachakra
path which correspond to the exhaustion of the material components of
the body and their energies at the six chakra-centresó.
I pray to my glorious lama.
You have fully realised the five wisdoms,
And have completely transformed the eight objects
of dualistic conception
By abiding for a single moment in non-dual primordial awareness.
Please bless me!
The five wisdoms of a Buddha are unveiled as the five aggregates
are purified. They include: the wisdom of all-encompassing space,
the mirror-like wisdom, the wisdom of equanimity, the wisdom of
discrimination and the all-accomplishing wisdom. The eight objects of
dualistic conception are the objects of the eight sense consciousnesses
- that of the five senses, the mind, the deluded mind and the foundation
consciousness. Once purified, these objects are transformed into the
eight female bodhisattvas, while the consciousnesses themselves are
transformed into the eight male bodhisattvas. All of this, however, is
merely a dsplay of the glorious lama who abides in non-dual primordial
awareness.
I pray to my glorious lama.
Your enlightened activity is one with the activity all the lamas,
Liberating and maturing fortunate disciples through
60 The twelve paths are equivalent to the bodhisattva path of insight up to
the path of no more learning. At each of these stages, 3,600 red and white essences
are retained at a particular chakra-centre, 3,600 moments of immutable bliss are
experienced, and 3,600 material components of the body are exhausted along with
3,600 active energies. Further details can be found in chapter 23 of Unveiling Your
Sacred Truth: The Tantric Path to Liberation.
287



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
the twelve empowered attainments
Of the generation and completion stages.
Please bless me!
As the lama embodies all the masters, the lama's compassionate activity
is one with the activity of all the lamas and leads to the liberation and
spiritual maturation of all his fortunate disciples. The scope of this
compassionate activity increases as one moves though the twelve
empowered attainments of the generation and completion stages. These
twelve attainments occur during the practice of the sixth yoga (of the
completion stage) and correspond to the exhaustion of the material
components of the body and their energies at the six chakra-centres.
Empowerments from innumerable Buddhas are needed to accomplish
each of these attainments.
I pray to the glorious lama.
You are one with all the yidams,
Your aggregates are the six Buddha-families,
Your consciousnesses are the eight bodhisattvas,
Your arms, legs and so forth are the assembly of wrathful deities.
Please bless me!
In this verse we supplicate the lama as the embodiment of all the yidams,
the peaceful and wrathful enlightened deities who are the source of all
tantric attainments. The six Buddha-families are the pure aspect of the
six aggregates, and they include the families of Amitabha, Akshobhya,
Ratnasambhava, Vairochana, Amoghasiddhi and Vajrasattva. The eight
bodhisattvas61 are the pure aspect of the eight consciousnesses, while
the assembly of wrathful deities are the pure aspect of the (six) action
faculties: the mouth, arms, legs, anus, urinary faculty and regenerative
faculty.
I pray to the glorious lama.
You are one with all the Buddhas,
Your nature is the magnificent body of truth.
You have perfected the two accumulations and manifest countless
emanations for the benefit of beings.
Please bless me!
61 The eight bodhisattvas include: Manjushri, Vajrapani, Avalokiteshvara,
Kshitigarbha, Sarvanivaranaviskambini, Akashagarbha, Maitreya and Samantabhadra.

2

HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
We now supplicate the lama as the embodiment of all the Buddhas.
His nature is inseparable from the dharmakaya, the magnificent body
of truth, and as he has perfected the two accumulations of wisdom and
merit, he is able to manifest countless emanation (bodies) for the benefit
of beings. Through accumulating wisdom and merit in this way he has
unveiled the two Buddha-kayas – the dharmakaya truth body and the
rupakaya form body.
I pray to the glorious lama.
You are one with all immaculate dharmas,
You manifest as the teachings and texts of ultimate meaning,
You lead us to the inexpressible profound truth.
Please bless me!
With this verse we consider the lama to be the embodiment of all
immaculate dharmas, which include the 84,000 teachings of the Buddha
which serve as a remedy for every conceivable mental affliction. This
includes the teachings and texts of ultimate meaning, which refer to
those teachings which are definitive in their interpretation, especially the
teachings of the third turning which describe the inconceivable reality of
Buddha-nature and form the basis of Dolpopa's undefeatable Shentong
view. Through the words and exposition of these teachings and texts, we
are led to the direct experience of the inexpressible profound truth, just
as a finger can point to the moon even though it is not the moon itself.
I pray to the glorious lama.
You are one with all the great lords of the Arya Sangha who abide in
the ten bodhisattva grounds,
Having attained complete liberation and accomplishment;
You are the immaculate virtuous friends, a refuge for all beings.
Please bless me!
We now supplicate the lama as the embodiment of the great lords of
the Arya Sangha, the immaculate virtuous friends who assist us on our
spiritual path. These are noble beings who have entered the path of
insight, where the true empty nature of reality is seen directly, and who
progress irreversibly towards Buddhahood through the power of their
merit and wisdom. This journey takes place in ten stages known as the
ten bodhisattva grounds, during which subtler and subtler obscurations
are overcome and qualities such as generosity and patience are perfected.
Complete. liberation and accomplishment refers to the freedom from
taking rebirth in samsara which is achieved on the path of insight, and
ICT
289



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
the attainment of the bodhisattva view of emptiness.
I pray to the glorious lama.
You are one with all the dharma protectors who destroy
all enemies and obstacles
Through the power of your non-dual compassion.
Please bless me!
Here we regard the lama as the embodiment of all the dharma protectors
who destroy all enemies and obstacles. These are worldly or enlightened
beings who take on a wrathful form, and their function is to protect
the Buddha's teachings from becoming diluted or distorted and to help
genuine practitioners overcome enemies and obstacles, which can either
be external (such as poor health or other circumstances which prevent
you from practicing), or internal (such as distorted views or being pulled
towards distracting activities). Non-dual compassion refers to the kind
compassion which is simultaneously aware of the illusory nature of all
phenomena and is therefore not bound by expectations or clinging.
I pray to the glorious lama.
You are the origin of all siddhis,
Bestower of both supreme and common accomplishments,
As you have mastered the actions of pacifying, expanding,
controlling and subduing.
Please bless me!
Now we supplicate the lama as the origin of all siddhis, as through
following his instructions we are able to attain both supreme and common
accomplishments. Common accomplishments refer to supernatural
abilities such as clairvoyance and miraculous powers while supreme
accomplishments are to do with enlightened qualities. The actions of
pacifying, expanding, controlling and subduing are known as the four
sublime powers of a Buddha, and these are the means by which a Buddha
spontaneously engages in activities which bring limitless benefit to
beings. As a Vajrayana practitioner you are training yourself to see that
everything the lama does or says is an expression of these four powers,
as you are learning to see him as a living Buddha.
I pray to the glorious lama.
You dispel all darkness
As you clear away wrong views by composing,
debating and explaining the sutras, tantras,
treatises and heart instructions.
290



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
LAMA
UL
Please bless me!
We now supplicate the lama in the aspect of a perfect Dharma teacher
who dispels the darkness of ignorance and wrong views. He does so by
composing texts, engaging in debate to defeat wrong views, explaining
the words of the Buddha as presented in the sutras and tantras with
reference to authentic treatises or commentaries, and finally by passing
on pith instructions or heart advice, which are key oral instructions
passed down through the lineage.
By drinking the nectar of his precious Dharma instruction
on the profound meaning,
From this day onwards may I follow the lama like a shadow.
May my glorious lama bless me so that this is accomplished!
This verse is a statement of our resolute commitment to follow the
lama's precious Dharma instructions which lead to the profound
truth of emptiness. As this Dharma is so precious, we also commit to
making offerings and serving the lama, following him like a shadow. By
strengthening our connection with the lama in this way we can accumulate
merit, putting us in a better position to understand the profound meaning
of his teachings.
Without consideration for food, clothing and luxuries,
Having abandoned wrong and impure livelihoods,
May I taste the nectar of Dharma with the tip of my tongue.
May my glorious lama bless me so that this is accomplished!
We now commit to developing a genuine mind of renunciation by
pledging to practise Dharma without consideration for food, clothing
and luxuries. This pledge is supported by our abandonment of wrong and
impure livelihoods, which includes any activity that involves harming
life, cheating, stealing, lying or other forms of immoral conduct.
From this day onwards may I remain in an isolated place,
Meditating single-pointedly upon the profound meaning,
So I may reach the great seal of liberation in this very lifetime.
May my glorious lama bless me so that this is accomplished!
Having established the mind of renunciation, we now pledge to simplify
our life and be content to dwell in an isolated place where conditions
are conducive to developing good single-pointed concentration and
meditating intensively upon the profound meaning of the Dharma. With
291



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
this kind of dedication we can aim to reach the great seal of liberation,
or the final result of Buddhahood, in a single lifetime.
May I see the four syllables at the chakras of the lama's body as the
four Buddha-kayas.
May I receive the four empowerments by focusing upon them.
May my glorious lama bless me so that this is accomplished!
This verse is an aspiration prayer to receive the four empowerments
from the lama. These four empowerments are received when you focus
on the four syllables located on the four main chakras of the lama's
body – the forehead, throat, heart and navel-centre. With each of these
empowerments you are awakening the four Buddha-kayas within
your mindstream – the nirmanakaya, sambhogakaya, dharmakaya and
svabhavikakaya.
(iii) Receiving the Four Empowerments
From the OM at my lama's forehead, a white OM streams forth and
dissolves into my own forehead chakra.
Through this power may I receive the vase empowerment.
May my glorious lama bless me so that this is accomplished!
As in the foundation guru yoga, we now receive the four empowerments.
This begins with the vase empowerment, which takes place as the OM
you visualise at the lama's forehead emanates dazzling white light and
dissolves into your own forehad chakra.
Through this power may I purify the obscurations of the body and
waking state,
Experience the four joys and unveil the vajra emanation body.
May my glorious lama bless me so that this is accomplished!
This vase empowerment purifies the obscurations of (your) body which
have been accumulated through negative actions such as stealing and
so forth, as well as the obscurations of the waking state, at which time
the forehead chakra is most active. The four joys are experienced when
the coarse bodily fluids are refined and become more and more subtle
at each of the four main chakras, and this also destroys the negativity
or obscurations which form ‘knots' around these chakras. In addition,
292



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
this empowerment introduces you to the indestructible vajra emanation
body, or the nirmanakaya aspect of your Buddha-nature.
From the AH at my lama's throat, a red AH streams forth and
dissolves into my own throat chakra.
Through this power may I receive the secret empowerment.
May my glorious lama bless me so that this is accomplished!
Next you receive the secret empowerment as dazzling red rays of light
stream forth from the AH syllable at the lama's throat and dissolve into
your own throat chakra.
Through this power may I purify the obscurations of speech
and the dream state,
Experience the four excellent joys and unveil the enjoyment
body of vajra speech.
May my glorious lama bless me so that this is accomplished!
This empowerment purifies the obscurations of speech connected with
lying, harsh words and so forth and also purifies the obscurations of the
dream state, which is associated with the throat chakra and determines
our ability to engage in practices such as dream yoga62. The four excellent
joys are experienced as the subtle fluids or essences are refined further,
and you are introduced to the enjoyment body of vajra speech, which is
the sambhogakaya aspect of your Buddha-nature.
From the HUM at my lama's heart, a black HUM streams forth and
dissolves into my own heart chakra.
Through this power may I receive the primordial wisdom
empowerment.
May my glorious lama bless me so that this is accomplished!
Now you receive the primordial wisdom empowerment as dazzling black
rays of light stream forth from the HUM syllable at the lama's heart and
dissolve into your own heart chakra.
Through this power may I purify the obscurations of mind
and the deep sleep state,
Experience the four supreme joys and unveil
the dharmakaya truth body of vajra mind.
May my glorious lama bless me so that this is accomplished!
O
62 The practice of dream yoga, also known as lucid dreaming, is described in
chapter 24 of Unveiling Your Sacred Truth: The Six-fold Cycle of Life and Rebirth.
293



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
This empowerment purifies the obscurations of mind connected with
lust, wrong views and so forth and also purifies the obscurations of the
deep sleep state, which is associated with the heart chakra.
The four supreme joys are experienced as an even subtler refinement
of the essences which takes place at the four chakras, and you are
introduced to the dharmakaya truth body of vajra mind, which is the
unborn dharmakaya aspect of your Buddha-nature.
From the HO at my lama's navel, a yellow HO streams forth
and dissolves into my own navel chakra.
Through this power may I receive the sacred fourth empowerment.
May my glorious lama bless me so that this is accomplished!
Finally you receive the sacred fourth empowerment as dazzling yellow
rays of light stream forth from the HO syllable at the lama's heart and
dissolve into your own navel chakra.
Through this power may I purify the propensities of attachment,
Experience the four innate joys and unveil the primordial vajra
wisdom of blissful emptiness.
May my glorious lama bless me so that this is accomplished!
This empowerment purifies the most subtle propensities of attachment
which are stored in the foundation consciousness and underlie all the
other negative tendencies of body, speech and mind. The four innate
joys are experienced as the most subtle refinement of the essences, and
you are introduced to the primordial vajra wisdom of blissful emptiness,
which is the svabhavikaya aspect of your Buddha-nature, representing
all three kayas together.
The lama at my crown melts into light and dissolves into me.
He abides in the centre of an eight-petalled lotus at my heart.
May my glorious lama bless me so that this is accomplished!
As in the foundation guru yoga, you end the practice by dissolving the
visualisation and recognising that the the ultimate lama is none other
than your own mind. To do this you watch the lama at (your) crown
melt into light and travel down your central channel to the centre of
an eight-petalled lotus at (your) heart. You should simply watch the
inseparability of the lama and your own mind, and when you are no
longer able to remain in this natural state you should return to making
prayers and supplications.
294



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
(iv) Dedication
Through this practice, may all beings purify all their stains and
obstacles and swiftly reach the essence of the Tathagata.
As with any practice, we conclude by dedicating the merit for the
ultimate benefit of others. In this case we pray that all beings purify
all their stains and obstacles which prevent them from recognising the
truth of their Buddha-nature. We also pray that they swiftly reach the
essence of the Tathagata, at which point the ground of our true being, the
Tathagatagharba, is completely unveiled.
This text, known as 'Guru Yoga - Rain of Blessings for the Six Yogas of
the Vajra Lineage', was composed by the dharma lord Kunkyen Dolpopa
Tonpa Jhiden Sherab Gyaltsen Palzangpo. May it lead to virtue and
auspiciousness!
This guru yoga practice text was composed by the omniscient Dolpopa
Sherab Gyaltsen, the most renowned master of the Jonang tradition,
known for combining the Kalachakra practice with the incomparable
Shentong view. Even during the present time this practice text is recited,
helping practitioners connect with the precious spiritual lineage that
Dolopa established.

Introduction
The Taranatha guru yoga is
the third of the three guru
yoga practices in the Jonang
tradition, and is also briefer
than the other two practices.
It is called the Anchor for
Collecting Siddhis as it
is a fundamental or root
practice (an “anchor')
for achieving spiritual
realisation. "Siddhis'
refers both to ordinary
spiritual attainments
such as clairvoyance or
miraculous powers, as well
as the supreme attainment
of enlightenment. We can
only uproot our mental
afflictions with enlightened
realisation, and this is why
Jetsun Taranatha
it is considered supreme.
As Taranatha was an extraordinary figure in the Jonang Kalachakra
lineage, this guru yoga gives us the opportunity to connect with his
spiritual presence and thereby make a link with all enlightened beings.
Nowadays in Jonang monasteries this guru yoga is performed in the
second week of an intensive three week guru yoga practice. We should
bear in mind that this is not just a preliminary practice, as it is through
guru yoga that we establish a strong connection to the lineage, and
without this all subsequent practices such as the Six Vajra Yogas are not
.

*
.

28

.

HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
effective toward rich enlightenment. Therefore guru yoga is the door to
tantric realisation and the heart essence of all tantric practice.
The basic principles and structure of this practice are the same as in the
foundation guru yoga, details of which are described earlier. What is most
important is that you remember that ultimately the lama is the wisdom
aspect of your own mind, and the act of praying to and supplicating
the external lama is actually a skilfull 'trick' to help you see this inner
wisdom.
The Practice and Commentary
(i) Visualisation
OM SVASTI
The ‘Anchor for Collecting Siddhis'guru yoga.
I fervently pay homage to the glorious lama.
All phenomena are merely mental fabrications,
While our Buddha-mind is indestructible - clear,
empty and beyond description.
All that we perceive is the endless display of the mind's projections,
Yet this clear, cognisant awareness is constant and unchanging.
This guru yoga begins by paying homage or “prostrating' to the glorious
lama, who is the embodiment of all the Buddhas and your personal
connection to enlightenment. We then describe the emptiness of relative
truth, stating how all relative phenomena are merely mental fabrications.
The ultimate truth of our Buddha-mind, however, is not empty of itself
but rather indestructible, clear, cognisant and unchanging. All that we
perceive is therefore a display of the mind's projections and not the true
nature of mind itself.
CTY
OM SHUNYATA JÑANA VAJRA SVABHAVA ATMA KHO HANG.
1
With this mantra all relative phenomena dissolve into the state of
emptiness (SHUNYATA), appearing like the reflection of the moon in
still water. Unlike the previous mantras, this mantra points to more than
297



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
-
just emptiness as it places greater emphasis on the ‘fullness' aspect - the
reality of Buddha-nature as the ground of our being.
My mind in its natural state is the pure realm of Akanishta.
In the centre of this pure realm is a radiant palace,
And in it my glorious root lama is seated on a lion
throne upon a lotus, sun and moon disc.
After resting the mind in its natural state for a while, you begin by
visualising a radiant palace in the centre of Akanishta, the pure realm
of the samboghakaya enjoyment body. The glorious root lama is seated
in the centre of this palace upon a lion throne, lotus flower, sun disc and
moon disc, in the sky before you. This signifies majesty, purity, wisdom
and compassion.
My glorious lama is radiant like a golden mountain
reflecting a hundred-thousand rays of sunlight.
He is pleased and smiles at me.
The lama is radiant in appearance and smiles at you, as if to say 'well
done’. The form of the lama is not specified here – you can visualise
him as Vajradhara, or alternatively you can visualise him in the form of
Taranatha or even the physical form of your root lama. In either case,
his nature is inseparable from the spiritual presence of Taranatha and the
nature of your own root lama.
Above my lama the lineage masters miraculously appear,
Surrounded by herukas such as Vajravarahi and clouds of yidams.
The masters of the Jonang-Shambala lineage appear above the lama
while peaceful and wrathful yidam deities (or herukas) surround the
lama like a great cloud.
Buddhas and bodhisattvas from the ten directions appear in the
space before me and glorious arhat emanations occupy the ground.
They are surrounded by dakinis and all-seeing dharma protectors
with their retinues, poised to obey the lama's every instruction.
We are now building the assembly to include all the Buddhas and
bodhisattvas from the ten directions (the four cardinal directions, the
four intermediate directions, up and down). We also visualise arhat
emanations, whom we consider to be not just arhats but actual emanations
of Buddhas and bodhisattvas. Surrounding these are dakinis and dharma
protectors, whose function is to guard us against internal and external
obstacles. They are poised to obey the lama's every instruction as they
d.
298



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
are in fact emanations of the lama which perform a particular role.
The entire assembly is in vibrant motion like lightning and storm-
clouds,
Filling all of space and the surrounding lands.
All these beings have radiant bodies;
They ceaselessly expound the Mahayana teachings
and their minds abide in the clear-light of great bliss
As they spontaneously perform oceans of virtuous activities.
This verse describes the visualised assembly in general terms. Rather
than being flat, solid or fixed, the assembly is radiant, in vibrant motion
and incredibly vast, extending to the furthest reaches of space. While
their minds abide in the clear-light of great bliss which is beyond all
dualistic notions, they ceaselessly expound the Mahayana teachings for
the benefit of all beings and they effortlessly and spontaneously perform
oceans of virtuous activities.
All of this is but a manifestation of the glorious lama,
Just as all appearances of samsara and nirvana are but a miraclulous
display of the lama's primordial wisdom.
The entire visualisation you have been building up is in fact a
manifestation of the glorious lama, since the lama is inseparable from
your own Buddha-mind and embodies all the lineage masters, yidams,
Buddhas, bodhisattvas, arhats, dakinis and dharma protectors. Of all
this sublime assembly we choose to focus on the lama since he is our
personal link to enlightenment.
According to the highest view of Buddhism, all appearances of samsara
and nirvana are a miraclulous display of the lama's primordial wisdom,
which is none other than our own Buddha-mind. On the ultimate level,
for example, the five aggregates are the five male Buddhas and the five
elements are their consorts, while the eight consciousnesses are the eight
male bodhisattvas and the eight objects represent their consorts.
(ii) Supplicating the Lama
I offer my body, my possessions, all the virtue of the three times
And every conceivable object of offering from all the pure-lands of
the ten directions.
Having established the visualisation with the lama as your central object
299

.....HAN
BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
of refuge, you now fill your mind with every conceivable object of
offering, including your body (your most cherished possession), your
possessions and all the virtuous deeds carried out by yourself and others
during the past, present and future. In addition, you should also visualise
the pure Buddha-realms of the ten directions and offer them up as well.
I offer everything my mind can conceive with pure aspiration:
All beings of the six realms including adversaries, friends and
relatives, extending to the furthest reaches of space,
Together with every pleasing object of offering in all of the three
realms.
Through the power of my visualisation and prayer,
I manifest all of these countless, inconceivable and magnificent
objects of offering.
The offering practice continues as you bring to mind and manifest
countless, inconceivable and magnificent objects of offering, all with the
pure aspiration of connecting to the Buddha's wisdom and benefiting
others. Your offering includes all beings of the six realms - human beings
and animals as well as unseen beings such as gods, demi-gods, hungry
ghosts and hell beings. You should also include your loved ones, friends,
relatives and adversaries. Normally in offering practices we only think of
pleasing or likeable objects, yet in reality there is no distinction between
pleasant and unpleasant as they are all merely a projection of the mind.
We should therefore offer everything without bias or judgment, letting
go of all our attachment and aversion.
All these offering treasures manifest from the primordial awareness
of the Buddhas, bodhisattvas and dakinis who appear in the three
times and ten directions.
All these innumerable and inconceivable manifestations are none
other than the glorious display of the lama's mind, inseparable from
my own mind,
The unborn display of dharmakaya.
This verse poses the question of where all of these offering objects come
from. Ultimately they all manifest from the primordial awareness of the
Buddhas and other objects of refuge, and in particular they are none
other than the glorious display of the lama's mind, which is inseparable
from my own mind. Thus we begin by conceiving the vast display of
offering objects as something outside of ourselves, and then recognise
that it is all a reflection of our own Buddha-nature which is inseparable
IU

from the lama.
Precious lama, you embody all the Buddhas.
Precious lama, you embody all the Dharmas.
Precious lama, you embody all the Sangha.
Supreme Dharma King, you embody all the lamas.
We now supplicate the lama as the embodiment of the Three Jewels - the
Buddha, Dharma and Sangha. We also pray to him as a supreme Dharma
King, embodying all the lamas who hold the holy lineage and teach the
precious Dharma.
You embody all the yidams while all the dakinis
and dharma protectors manifest as your envoys.
I pray to you Vajradhara,
Please bless me and all those who have faith in you!
We now pray to the lama as the embodiment of the ‘inner Three Jewels',
which include the enlightened yidam deities who are the root of spiritual
progress, the dakinis who are the root of enlightened activity and an
inner source of protection, and the dharma protectors who protect
against all obstacles to spiritual progress. We say they manifest as (the
lama's) envoys since while they are inseparable from the enlightened
nature of the lama, on a relative level they are sent forth to accomplish
the lama's instructions like the messenger of a king. Finally we pray to
the lama as Vajradhara, who is the tantric form of the enlightened guru
and the source of all blessings.
Glorious lama, you are Vajradhara in the pure realm
of the enjoyment body.
You are the wrathful Heruka when subduing all evils.
You are Shakyamuni to beings with pure renunciation.
You are the great sage to the ascetics.
Just as a crystal can reflect many different colours, the compassion
of the glorious lama is reflected in countless forms depending on the
merit, capacities and personalities of different beings. For those with
pure perception he appears as Vajradhara in the pure realm of the
enjoyment body and for unruly or unwholesome beings who need to be
tamed he appears as the wrathful Heruka, an enlightened expression of
wrathful compassion who is able to subdue all evils. For those with pure
renunciation, such as the great arhats of the Buddha's time, he appears
in the human form of Buddha Shakyamuni, and for those who live as
301



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
-
---
ascetics he appears as a great sage who points out the true middle path.
To those who follow the path of the three vehicles,
You manifest as the Bodhisattva, the Pratyeka
and the great Shravaka.
You also appear in the form of Brahma, Vishnu, Lord Shiva
and all other sages and saints.
The Buddha described three types of paths to suit different types of
spiritual aspirants, which are referred to as the three vehicles – the
Bodhisattva vehicle, the Pratyeka vehicle and the Shravaka vehicle63.
The Bodhisattva vehicle is a journey over a vast number of lifetimes
to fulfill the vow to become an omniscient Buddha, so that we can
spontaneously and effortlessly help beings be free from suffering and
attain enlightenment themselves. The Pratyeka or 'solitary realiser'
vehicle is a path to developing deep wisdom through one's own analysis
without the need for external teachers, resulting in a more limited form
of enlightenment. The Shravaka or “hearer' vehicle involves hearing
and following the Buddha's basic teachings and achieving individual
liberation from samsara. For aspirants on each of these paths, the
lama manifests as an appropriate spiritual mentor, whether this be a
Bodhisattva, Pratyeka (or) great Shravaka.
The final line of this verse is testament to the depth of Taranatha's
wisdom and his perfect non-sectarian outlook. Not only does the lama
manifest as Buddhist teachers or mentors, but also as teachers, sages
and saints from other traditions such as Brahma, Vishnu and Lord Shiva;
this may even include Jesus Christ or the great prophet Mohammed. As
beings have a countless variety of personalities and learning styles, it
makes sense that the Buddhas would teach a variety of religious systems
in order to lead them all closer to the truth.
Sometimes you appear in the position of a king,
At other times you appear as a yogi or ascetic.
To others you appear as a pure monk with simple robes.
I pray to you, performer of great, vast deeds according to
the needs of each being.
63 More about the different vehicles or spiritual paths within Buddhism can be
found in chapter 23 of Unveiling Your Sacred Truth: The Seven Progressive Vehicles of
the Buddhist Path.
302



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
UZ
Just as the thoughts and aspirations
of all beings are inconceivable,
So too is the vastness and depth of your teachings.
In this verse we continue to supplicate the lama as the supreme
embodiment of everything which is beneficial in the world. He appears
in the position of a king who is keen on worldly affairs, in order to bring
peace, justice and spiritual values to a great number of people. He also
appears as a yogi or ascetic to demonstrate the path of renunciation and
discipline to spiritual aspirants, and as a pure monk with simple robes
to demonstrate perfect moral conduct and the benefits of a simple life
focused on others' benefit.
We therefore pray to the lama who performs great, vast deeds according
to the needs of each being. In the same way that the thoughts and
aspirations of all beings are inconceivable, so too are the lama's methods
of teaching the Dharma.
Just as rainbows and clouds appear in the sky,
Arising, abiding and then vanishing back into the sky...
You are the dharmakaya truth body free from all extremes,
Performing great deeds spontaneously and without effort.
Even though you act in a way that meets the needs of all beings,
You abide in a state of non-dual natural purity.
These two verses offer a poetic description of the lama's spontaneous
and effortless compassion, which takes the form of great deeds
performed in a way that meet the needs of all beings. These spontaneous
activities are likened to rainbows and clouds which arise and then vanish
spontaneously into the vast expanse of the sky, depending on numerous
causes and conditions such as the presence of moisture, the angle of the
sunlight and so forth. In the same way, the lama's great deeds emerge
from the vast expanse of the dharmakaya triuth body, or the state of
non-dual natural purity, depending on causes and conditions such as the
merit and aspirations of different beings.
You are beyond birth and death, coming and going, near and far.
I pray to you, pristine truth body.
I pay homage from the depths of my heart with unceasing devotion!
The pristine dharmakaya truth body of the lama is completely beyond all
concepts such as birth and death, coming and going, near and far. The
303



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
unceasing devotion that we arouse towards the lama from the depths of
our heart is none other than devotion and confidence in the truth of our
own Buddha-nature; praying to the lama is therefore a skilful “trick’ to
bring us closer to this sacred truth.
Precious lama, you embody all sources of refuge.
I offer countless virtuous objects while being aware
of their empty nature.
I confess and purify all my negativities even though
their nature is pure from the beginning.
With this verse we begin a seven-branch prayer. First we pay homage to
the lama who embodies all sources of refuge, and then we offer countless
virtuous objects and confess and purify all our negativities. It carries
a deeper meaning, however, as we are called to be aware of the empty
nature of the offering objects and that ultimately there is nothing to
confess as our nature is primordially pure These incredibly profound
statements help us view the practice in the light of ultimate truth as they
remind us of the illusory nature of all phenomena.
I rejoice in the virtue of all beings in samsara and nirvana.
May the empty sound of your teachings never cease.
The seven-branch prayer continues as we rejoice in the virtue of all beings
and request that the lama never cease teaching the precious Dharma.
From the perspective of ultimate truth, however, even the lama's words
are none other than empty sound, a reflection of the unborn dharmakaya
in the form of sound.
May you ceaselessly turn the wheel of precious Dharma.
May you remain forever for the sake of all beings.
With this verse we request that the lama ceaselessly turn the wheel of
precious Dharma according to the needs of sentient beings, and that he
remains forever for the sake of all beings without abandoning samsara.
I dedicate all my virtue so my mind may become inseparable
from yours, o holy lama.
May all beings attain supreme enlightenment!
The seven-branch prayer ends here as we dedicate all our virtue so that
our mind may become inseparable from the mind of the holy lama,
meaning that we will discover the sacred truth of our own Buddha-
nature by recognising the ultimate nature of the lama. We also dedicate
304



HIDDEN TREASURE OF THE PROFOUND PATH
MG -
this practice with the aspiration of a bodisattva, wishing with great
compassion that all beings be free from suffering and attain supreme
enlightenment.
(iii) Receiving the Four Empowerments
Glorious Drolway Gonpo, rescuer of all beings,
Please bless me with your body, speech and mind.
Bestow upon me the four empowerments at this very instant!
We now supplicate glorious Drolway Gonpo, better known as Taranatha,
who is the rescuer of all beings from the uncontrollable suffering of
samsaric existence. We implore him to bless us with his body, speech
and mind and bestow the four empowerments upon us. As the verse
mentions Taranatha (the author of this guru yoga practice), it must have
been added by someone else after Taranatha's time.
May my body transform into innate bliss.
May my speech transform with the power of mantra.
May my heart transform into clear-light wisdom!
When we receive the first three of the four empowerments our body
transforms into the vajra body of innate bliss, our speech transforms
into the vajra speech which possesses the power of mantra, and our heart
transforms into the vajra mind which is inseparable from the clear-light
wisdom of our Buddha-nature. This verse also implies a deeper level of
meaning which accords with the 'secret’instructions of tantra, especially
the reference to the power of mantra.
Glorious lama, I pray to you to bless me at this very instant.
Rays of light stream forth from your forehead, throat,
heart, and navel,
And then dissolve into my own four chakras.
Please bestow upon me the four empowerments of body,
speech, mind and primordial vajra wisdom!
As you recite this verse you begin to receive the four empowerments.
Brilliant rays of white light stream forth from the lama's forehead, while
dazzling rays of red, black and yellow light stream forth from the three
305



BY KHENTRUL RINPOCHE
other centres – the throat, heart and navel centre. These rays of light
dissolve into your own four chakras as you receive the empowerments
of body, speech, mind and primordial vajra wisdom. With each of these
four empowerments particular defilements are purified and particular
spiritual powers are attained; these are described in previous sections
of this text.
May I receive the vase empowerment.
May I receive the secret empowerment.
May I receive the union of great bliss and wisdom empowerment.
May I receive the sacred fourth empowerment of
the great seal beyond conception!
With this verse you actually receive the four empowerments – the
vase, secret, wisdom and sacred fourth empowerment. Each of these
points to a particular aspect of your Buddha-nature, as if to say “You
have that!' The third empowerment here is literally translated as the
“empowerment of the union of great bliss and primordial wisdom”. The
fourth empowerment is described as the great seal beyond conception
as it directly points out the ultimate truth of your Buddha-nature which
is completely beyond all dualistic notions that give rise to conceptual
thought.
Great Dharma King, I rely on no-one else but you,
You are my only true refuge.
Just like water poured into water,
May I dissolve into inseparable union with you!
For one last time we are proclaiming our complete trust in the lama who
we regard as a great Dharma King and our only true (object of) refuge
or our only worthy rescuer from the pain of samsara. The lama then
dissolves into light and becomes inseparably mixed with your mind-
stream just like water being poured into water. With more experience,
however, this dissolving process may be more like a vase shattering
as the empty space inside the vase merges with the outside space. By
repeating this exercise again and again and simply watching the mind of
the lama and your own mind come together like this, you can gain great
confidence in the reality of your Buddha-nature which has been with you
all along
May the lama melt into the essence of nectar and fill
my four chakras,

Bestowing empowerment upon me...
As the lama melts into light and dissolves into you, you can visualise his
essence in the form of blissful, radiant white nectar filling your forehead,
throat, heart and navel chakras, thus purifying all the defilements and
bad energies stored around these chakras. Incredible joy is experienced
as these energy-centres are activated, and you are empowered once again
with the blessings of the lama's body, speech, mind and primordial
wisdom.
Meditate on the natural lama, the great truth body inseparable
from your own mind, and remain in the natural state beyond all
concepts.
[Remain in this state for as long as you can].
Once again you should meditate on the inseparability of the great truth
body of the lama and your own mind. We call this the natural lama, the
natural (enlightened) state beyond all dualistic notions which can only
be realised when our faith and devotion take us beyond the ordinary
mental mind.
This is the perfect guru yoga enabling you to reach Buddhahood
in one lifetime. Have no doubt.
Composed by Jetsun Taranatha, aged 29.
This practice was composed by the great Jonang scholar and siddha
Jetsun Taranatha in the early 17th century. His concluding statement
reminds us that this guru yoga practice is supremely profound, rare
and precious, as it forges a connection to the holy lineage of the Six
Vajra Yogas. This is such an effective and powerful practice that it can
enable you to attain the omniscient state of Buddhahood in a single
lifetime, emulating many great practitioners of the past. This should be
a tremendous source of confidence, and you should therefore have no
doubt about this practice.
